New complexities in helper T Cell fate determination and the implications for autoimmune diseases.
Abstract.
Recently, new complexities in cell fate decision for helper T cells have emerged.
One new lineage, which has come to be called Th17 cells, selectively produces proinflammatory cytokines including interleukin-17 -LRB- IL-17, A and F -RRB-, IL-21, and IL-22.
In conjunction with transforming growth factor ß-1 -LRB- TGFß-1 -RRB-, IL-6, IL-21, and IL-23, which activate the transcription factor, signal transducer, and activator of transcription 3 -LRB- Stat3 -RRB-, the expression of another transcription factor, retinoic acid-related orphan receptor-γt -LRB- RORγt -RRB- leads to the differentiation of Th17 cells in mice.
Other cytokines including IL-2, IL-4, interferon-γ -LRB- IFN-γ -RRB- and IL-27 inhibit Th17 differentiation.
However, IL-2 acting with TGFß-1 induces differentiation of naive CD4 + T cells to become regulatory T cells -LRB- Tregs -RRB-.
Th17 cells are now known to play an important role not only in the pathogenesis of inflammation and autoimmune diseases, but also host defense against extracellular bacteria.
Conversely, extensive data substantiate the role of Tregs as essential in maintenance of peripheral tolerance.
Keywords : Th17 cells, autoimmune diseases, inflammation, IL-17, Rheumatoid arthritis.
Introduction.
It is well-established that the innate immune response leads to activation of adaptive immunity, shaping the proper response, depending upon the pathogen eliciting the reaction.
Conversely, though, it is also clear that adaptive immune response, especially, CD4 + or helper T cells orchestrate responses to effectively eliminate pathogens.
Classically, helper T cells were considered to differentiate into two lineages, T helper 1 -LRB- Th1 -RRB- cells or Th2 cells -LRB- 1 -RRB-.
In addition to ligation of the T-cell receptor -LRB- TCR -RRB- and co-stimulatory receptors, a suitable cytokine milieu is required for fate decision of helper T cells -LRB- 1 -RRB-.
In particular, interleukin-12 -LRB- IL-12 -RRB-, which is produced by activated antigen-presenting cells -LRB- APCs -RRB-, promotes Th1 differentiation -LRB- 2 -RRB-, whereas IL-4, produced by activated T cells and some innate immune cells, drives Th2 differentiation -LRB- 1 -RRB-.
While the Th1/Th2 paradigm provided invaluable insights for immunologists, its limitations were also clear.
What was the most obvious was the inability of this dichotomy to explain autoimmune diseases.
More recent studies have shown the existence of the additional subpopulations of T helper cells that are also important in immunoregulation and host defense.
One important subset is CD4 + CD25 +, regulatory T cells -LRB- Tregs -RRB- -LRB- 3, 4 -RRB-.
Tregs suppress the proliferation and function of effector T cells, and attenuate immune responses against self or nonself-antigens -LRB- 3, 4 -RRB-.
Another recently identified new fate of T cells is Th17 cells that selectively produce IL-17 -LRB- A and F -RRB- -LRB- 5, 6 -RRB-.
In the past three years, discoveries pertaining to this newly identified T helper subset in humans and mice have accumulated with tremendous speed -LRB- 7-10 -RRB-.
In this review, we will discuss the historical developments that led to a new understanding of the role of T cells in autoimmune diseases and recent advances that have led to even newer insights into T cell biology.
Pathogenicity of IL-23, but not IL-12 in autoimmune diseases.
Th1 cells produce interferon-γ -LRB- IFN-γ -RRB- and lymphotoxin, and are responsible for protection against intracellular pathogens such as viruses, mycobacteria, and protozoa -LRB- 11 -RRB-.
Produced by activated APCs, IL-12 activates the transcription factor, signal transducer, and activator of transcription 4 -LRB- Stat4 -RRB- -LRB- 2 -RRB-.
Stat4-dependent signaling in conjunction with TCR-dependent signals induces the expression of T-box-expressed-in-T-cells -LRB- T-bet -RRB-, the so-called master regulator of Th1 differentiation -LRB- 2 -RRB-.
Recently, in humans, it has been shown that STAT4 polymorphisms are associated with rheumatoid arthritis -LRB- RA -RRB- and systemic lupus erythematosus -LRB- SLE -RRB- -LRB- 12 -RRB-.
IFN-γ also activates Stat1 which further induces T-bet to form an autocrine feedback loop for IFN-γ production -LRB- 2 -RRB-.
T-bet promotes not only IFN-γ production but also suppression of Th2 cytokines production by T cells -LRB- 2 -RRB-.
On the other hand, Th2 cells produce IL-4, IL-5, and IL-13 -LRB- 1 -RRB-.
IL-4 activates Stat6, which up-regulates the expression of GATA-binding protein 3 -LRB- GATA-3 -RRB- -LRB- 1 -RRB-.
Th2 cytokines are potent activators of B-cell Immunoglobulin E production, eosinophil recruitment, and mucosal expulsion mechanisms, and are essential for promoting host defense against helminths and other parasites -LRB- 1 -RRB-.
In addition, Th2 cells have been shown to mediate allergic diseases such as asthma, rhinitis, and atopic dermatitis -LRB- 11 -RRB-.
However, it was shown that IFN-γ deficiency exacerbated rather than ameliorated mouse models of autoimmune diseases such as experimental autoimmune encephalomyelitis -LRB- EAE -RRB- -LRB- 16 -RRB-.
Subsequently, a new cytokine, which consists of IL-23p19 and IL-12p40, was identified and termed IL-23 -LRB- 17 -RRB-.
Interestingly, the IL-23 receptor -LRB- IL-23R -RRB- forms dimers with the IL-12Rß1 chain shared by IL-12 and IL-23 -LRB- 18 -RRB-.
IL-23R is predominantly expressed on T and natural killer -LRB- NK -RRB- cells -LRB- 18, 19 -RRB-.
IL-23 activates Janus kinase 2 -LRB- Jak2 -RRB- and tyrosine kinase 2 -LRB- Tyk2 -RRB-, which in turn leads to activation of Stat1, Stat3, Stat4, and Stat5, among which Stat3 is the predominant factor phosphorylated by this cytokine -LRB- 17, 18 -RRB-.
Of note, IL-23p19-deficient mice or IL-12p40-deficient -LRB- IL-12 / IL-23-deficient -RRB- mice were resistant to collagen-induced arthritis -LRB- CIA -RRB- and EAE -LRB- 20, 21 -RRB-.
However, IL-12p35-deficient mice had increased susceptibility to CIA and EAE -LRB- 20, 21 -RRB-.
These studies directly negated the pathogenic role of the IL-12 / IFN-γ axis in autoimmunity.
This was an important piece of information that led to the unraveling of the Th1/Th2 paradigm as an explanation of autoimmunity.
Accordingly, additional studies on IL-23p19-deficient mice and the anti-IL-23p19 antibody revealed that IL-23, but not IL-12, was the culprit in autoimmunity, at least in mouse disease models -LRB- 21-23 -RRB-.
The pathogenic role of IL-23 was also confirmed by the phenotype of IL-23p19 transgenic mice, in which premature death, systemic inflammation, anemia, and elevated serum levels of inflammatory cytokines and acute phase proteins were observed -LRB- 22 -RRB-.
Therefore, IL-23 began to attract attention as a factor crucial to inflammation and autoimmune diseases.
The IL-23 / IL17 axis in inflammation.
While it was becoming clear that IL-23 was the culprit in autoimmune and inflammatory diseases, the question remained, how was it acting ?.
Another inflammatory cytokine, IL-17, was noted to be produced by activated purified T cells in the presence of LPS-stimulated dendritic cells -LRB- DCs -RRB- -LRB- 5 -RRB-.
It was also found that IL-23 promoted IL-17 production from memory T cells and this production was suppressed by treatment with anti-IL-12p40 antibody -LRB- 5 -RRB-.
Now IL-17 is recognized as the founding member of a family of proinflammatory cytokines : IL-17 -LRB- IL-17A -RRB-, IL-17B, IL-17C, IL-17D, IL-17E -LRB- known as IL-25 -RRB-, and IL-17F -LRB- 6 -RRB-.
IL-17A and IL-17F induce the production of various proinflammatory cytokines such as tumor necrosis factor-α -LRB- TNF - α -RRB-, IL-1ß, and IL-6, and CXC chemokines from monocytes, airway epithelial cells, vein endothelial cells, and fibroblasts to mount defense against extracellular bacteria such as Klebsiella pneumonia, Bacteroides fragilis, and Mycobacterium tuberculosis -LRB- 6, 25, 26 -RRB-.
These responses result in the recruitment, activation and migration of neutrophils to the sites of inflammation and infection -LRB- 6 -RRB-.
CD4 + T cells are major producers of IL-17, but in addition CD8 + T cells, neutrophils, γδ T cells, and invariant natural killer T -LRB- NKT -RRB- cells also produce this cytokine -LRB- 26-28 -RRB-.
Various reports associated IL-23 with IL-17 production with the onset or exacerbation of inflammation -LRB- 20-23, 29 -RRB-.
For instance, IL-23p19-deficient mice showed reduced incidence of CIA, with fewer IL-17-producing CD4 + T cells -LRB- 20 -RRB-.
Consistent with this report, treatment with anti-IL-23p19 antibody reduced serum levels of IL-17 and inhibited development of EAE -LRB- 29 -RRB-.
Moreover, IL-23 was found to be essential for production of IL-17 and IL-6 in colitis mouse models -LRB- 22, 23 -RRB-.
Regardless of exactly how IL-23 works, these reports supported the idea that an IL-23 / IL-17 axis, but not IL-12 / IFN-γ axis, was a crucial pathway in the pathogenesis of various autoimmune diseases -LRB- 21, 30 -RRB-.
Regulation of Th17 differentiation.
Although many results linked IL-23 with IL-17 production in CD4 + T cells, less was known about how Th17 cells arose from naive CD4 + T cells.
It was especially puzzling that naive CD4 + T cells did not express IL-23R -LRB- 18 -RRB-.
In a search for optinum culture condition for Th17 differentiation it was recognized that naive CD4 + T cells cultured with activated DCs produced IL-17 -LRB- 16 -RRB-.
It was then recognized that the combination of IL-6 and transforming growth factor ß-1 -LRB- TGFß-1 -RRB-, with appropriate stimulation of TCR, were the optinum stimuli inducing Th17 differentiation -LRB- Fig. 1a -RRB- -LRB- 16 -RRB-.
Accordingly, TGFß-1-deficient mice showed impaired Th17 development, whereas addition of TGFß-1 rescued the number of Th17 cells -LRB- 7, 33 -RRB-.
Thus it became clear that IL-23 was not the direct initiator of Th17 production -LRB- 16 -RRB-, but rather was an important factor for expanding and maintaining Th17 cells in vivo -LRB- 34 -RRB-.
New T cell lineages in mice -LRB- a -RRB- and humans -LRB- c -RRB-.
When stimulated by APCs such as DCs and macrophages, and cognate peptide, naive helper T cells differentiate into lineages determined by the cytokine milieu.
TGFß-1 is a critical factor in the differentiation of new two lineages in mice T cells.
In conjunction with TCR stimulation, the combination of TGFß-1 and IL-2 -LRB- and other γc cytokines -RRB- induces the expression of Foxp3, leading to the differentiation of naive CD4 + T cells into anti-inflammatory Tregs -LRB- a -RRB-.
However, in the presence of TGFß-1 with IL-6 or IL-21, which activates Stat3 and up-regulates RORγt, naive CD4 + T cells develop to become pro-inflammatory Th17 cells -LRB- a -RRB-.
Th17 differentiation is suppressed by IFN-γ, IL-4, IL-2, IL-25, IL-27, and retinoic acid in mice -LRB- b -RRB-.
Both Th17 cells and Tregs are also present in humans -LRB- c -RRB-.
TGFß-1, IL-1ß, and IL-2 in combination with IL-6, IL-21 or IL-23 are necessary for human Th17 differentiation -LRB- c -RRB-.
APCs, antigen-presenting cells ; iTregs, inducible Tregs.
Autocrine regulation of Th17 differentiation by IL-21.
In the classic Th1/Th2 paradigm, T cell subsets produce factors that promote their differentiation and constrain the differentiation of the opposing lineage.
It was of interest in this regard that the Th17 cells were found to selectively produce IL-21 -LRB- 35-38 -RRB-.
IL-21 has structural homology with IL-2 and IL-15, and the initial report showed the effects of IL-21 produced by CD4 + T cells and NKT cells on the proliferation and function of NK cells, B cells, and T cells -LRB- 39, 40 -RRB-.
Recently though, it has also been found that the autocrine production of IL-21 by Th17 cells promotes Th17 differentiation while inhibiting IFN-γ production -LRB- 35-38 -RRB-.
Accordingly, the deficiency of IL-21 -LRB- or its receptor -RRB-, or blocking of IL-21, attenuates the generation of Th17 cells -LRB- 35-37 -RRB-.
Transcription factors for Th17 differentiation.
To precisely understand the molecular mechanisms of Th17 differentiation, it is important to define the transcription factors that directly regulate IL-17 production.
All of IL-6, IL-21, and IL-23 activate the transcription factor Stat3 in T cells -LRB- 38, 41, 42 -RRB- ; accordingly, Th17 differentiation is abrogated in Stat3-deficient T cells -LRB- 38, 42-45 -RRB-.
Moreover, conditional deletion of Stat3 in T cells also abrogates the development of autoimmune diseases such as EAE and autoimmune pneumonitis in mice -LRB- 43 -RRB-.
In addition, IL-6 and IL-23 promote IL-23R expression and this also is Stat3-dependent -LRB- 10, 36, 37 -RRB-.
Recently, the importance of Stat3 in human Th17 differentiation has been documented -LRB- 46 -RRB-.
Like other T cell subsets, Th17 cells also have a lineage-specific transcription factor, namely the retinoic acid-related orphan receptor-γt -LRB- RORγt -RRB- -LRB- 8 -RRB-.
Interestingly, RORγt-deficient T cells produce fewer Th17 cells, whereas overexpression of RORγt in T cells promotes IL-17 expression -LRB- 8 -RRB-.
Recent studies have shown that RORγt expression is significantly reduced in Stat3-deficient T cells -LRB- 43-45 -RRB-.
Also, it has been shown that expression of another retinoic acid related nuclear receptor, RORα also induces Th17 differentiation -LRB- 47 -RRB-.
Counter-regulation of IL-17 and the Yin/Yang of Th17 cells and Tregs.
Indeed, it has been recognized that the Th1-related cytokine IFN-γ inhibits Th17 differentiation -LRB- 31, 32 -RRB-.
Consistent with this concept, T-bet-deficient mice show enhanced Th17 differentiation -LRB- 48 -RRB-.
Similarly, the Th2-related IL-4 is also shown to down-regulate Th17 differentiation -LRB- 49 -RRB-.
Interestingly, IL-27, an IL-12-related heterodimeric cytokine, also has anti-inflammatory effect by inhibiting the generation of Th17 lineage and leads to limitation of EAE -LRB- 50 -RRB-.
Like IFN-γ, IL-27 suppresses Th17 differentiation through a STAT1-dependent manner -LRB- 51, 52 -RRB-.
IL-25 -LRB- IL-17E -RRB- was also shown to inhibit IL-17 production by promoting Th2 differentiation -LRB- 53 -RRB-.
Another new subset of helper T cells that provides considerable insight into the pathogenesis of autoimmunity is the CD4 + CD25 + regulatory T cells -LRB- Tregs -RRB- -LRB- 3, 4, 54 -RRB-.
Tregs suppress proliferation of effector T cells and maintain self tolerance by down-regulating immune responses against self or nonself-antigens -LRB- 3, 4, 54 -RRB-.
Naturally arising Tregs -LRB- nTregs -RRB- are generated in the thymus, whereas inducible Tregs -LRB- iTregs -RRB- arise from naive T cells after antigen exposure and cytokine stimulation in the periphery, especially in the gut -LRB- 58 -RRB-.
Recently, it has been shown that CD4 + CD25 + T cells express the transcription factor, forkhead box protein 3 -LRB- Foxp3 -RRB-, which is necessary and sufficient for Tregs to develop and function -LRB- 59, 60 -RRB-.
In mice, IL-2 and TGFß-1 were able to differentiate CD4 + CD25 - naive T cells into CD4 + CD25 + Foxp3 + Tregs -LRB- 61, 62 -RRB-.
Therefore, the importance of TGFß-1 for both Tregs and Th17 lineage led to the speculation that these lineages were related.
In fact, IL-2 was found to inhibit the expression of RORγt while the enhancing expression of Foxp3 -LRB- 44 -RRB-.
Recently, it has been reported that TGFß-1 can promote either Th17 or Tregs lineage differentiation, depending on its local concentration -LRB- 63 -RRB-.
Further complexities of Th17 cells.
The roles of Th17 cells are complicated by the fact that these cells also have the ability to produce anti-inflammatory cytokines such as IL-10 -LRB- 34 -RRB-.
This cytokine has anti-inflammatory properties that suppress functions of DCs and macrophages -LRB- 64 -RRB-.
IL-10 can be produced by many cell types such as B cells, macrophages, DCs, Th2 cells, and distinct populations of Tregs -LRB- 64 -RRB-.
Recently, it has been reported that de-novo generation of Th17 cells in the presence of IL-6 and TGFß-1 leads to the production of IL-10 with up-regulation of RORγt and IL-17 -LRB- 34 -RRB-.
Furthermore, IL-1ß, but not IL-23, potentiates IL-10 production in Th17 cells along with IL-6 and TGFß-1 -LRB- 34 -RRB-.
Another cytokine produced by Th17 cells is IL-22 -LRB- 25, 65, 66 -RRB-.
IL-22 belongs to the IL-10 family of cytokines which include IL-19, IL-20, IL-24, and IL-26.
Expressed in activated T cells, Th1 cells and NK cells -LRB- 67 -RRB-, IL-22 induces expression of various antimicrobial peptides such as ß-defensins in skin, respiratory, and digestive tissues, which express IL-22R -LRB- 68 -RRB-.
In fact, expression of IL-22 and ß-defensins is higher in skin from patients with psoriasis and atopic dermatitis than in that from healthy individuals -LRB- 69 -RRB-.
While it is clear that IL-22 and IL-17 can contribute to host defense and to pathogenesis of various autoimmune diseases -LRB- 25 -RRB-, it is also notable that IL-22 also has important anti-inflammatory effects -LRB- 70 -RRB-.
Specifically, IL-22-expressing Th17 cells provided protection in models of hepatitis -LRB- 70 -RRB-.
Recently, IL-22 also has been shown not to be required for the development of EAE in mice -LRB- 71 -RRB-.
These facts indicate the complexity of Th17 cells, which produce multiple cytokines and have diverse functions during inflammation.
Human Th17 differentiation.
While a large body of evidence has documented that the best recipe for generating Th17 cells from murine naive CD4 + T cells is the combination of TGFß-1 and IL-6 or IL-21, several groups initially reported that the regulation of human Th17 differentiation was quite distinct -LRB- Fig. 1c -RRB- -LRB- 9, 10, 66, 72-74 -RRB-.
Specifically, TGFß-1 was initially considered to have inhibitory effect on human IL-17 production ; however, the role of TGFß-1 in human Th17 differentiation has recently become clearer.
While TGFß-1 alone had an inhibitory effect on production of IL-17 by T cells, culturing human naive CD4 + T cells from cord blood in serum-free medium revealed a requirement of TGFß-1 for Th17 differentiation -LRB- 72 -RRB-.
While TGFß-1 is required for the expression of RORγt in human naive CD4 + T cells from cord blood, TGFß-1 can inhibit the function of RORγt at high doses -LRB- 72 -RRB-.
However, inflammatory cytokines -LRB- IL-1ß, IL-6, and IL-21 or IL-23 -RRB- relieve the latter effect of TGFß-1 -LRB- 72 -RRB-.
By using serum-free medium it has thus been clarified that the optimum conditions for human Th17 differentiation are TGFß-1, IL-1ß, and IL-2 in combination with IL-6, IL-21 or IL-23 -LRB- 72-74 -RRB-.
A key aspect of Th17 regulation is the regulation of IL-23R -LRB- 10 -RRB-.
Naive CD4 + T cells express low levels of this receptor, but the combination of TGFß-1, IL-1ß, and IL-23 can strongly induce this receptor -LRB- 10, 72 -RRB-.
Thus, IL-23 promotes expression of its own receptor, allowing it to be an effective inducer of IL-17.
It is of note is that CCR6 + IL-23R + human memory CD4 + T cells are major producers of IL-17 -LRB- 75, 76 -RRB-.
Th17 cells in autoimmune diseases.
Following extensive analysis of mouse disease models such as EAE, CIA, and IBD, it has also become evident that IL-17 is a contributing factor in human autoimmune diseases.
For instance, perivascular IL-17-producing T cells are present in brain lesions of active MS patients and these cells are reduced in quiescent MS patients -LRB- 77 -RRB-.
Moreover, DCs from MS patients secrete more IL-23 than healthy controls, and T cells from MS patients secrete more IL-17 than healthy controls -LRB- 78 -RRB-.
Also, elevated levels of IL-17 have been noted in the sera and in tissues of patients with RA, IBD, and psoriasis -LRB- 25 -RRB-.
We will see more evidence confirming the roles of IL-17 in human diseases and inflammation in the future.
Recent genetic data has linked polymorphisms of the Il23r gene to various human diseases such as ankylosing spondylitis, CD, and psoriasis -LRB- 79-81 -RRB-.
Accordingly treating CD and psoriasis patients with anti-IL-12p40 antibody has resulted in some success -LRB- 14, 15 -RRB-.
Th17 cells in rheumatoid arthritis.
First, IL-17-deficient mice fail to develop CIA when challenged -LRB- 82 -RRB-.
Consistent with this, treatment with neutralizing IL-17 monoclonal antibody ameliorates joint inflammation in CIA models -LRB- 83 -RRB-.
Furthermore, it has been reported that active immunization using virus-like particles conjugated with recombinant IL-17 leads to high levels of anti-IL-17 antibodies in mice and reduces scores of disease severity in CIA -LRB- 84 -RRB-.
These results highlight the role of IL-17 as an exacerbation factor in rodent arthritis models.
In particular, IL-17 up-regulates the production of IL-1ß and TNF-α from APCs in arthritic joints -LRB- 86, 87 -RRB-.
Moreover, IL-17 induces IL-6, IL-8, and IL-23 from RA synovial fibroblasts and chemokines such as CCL20/MIP3 α from synoviocytes to induce migration of T cells and DCs into inflammatory lesions -LRB- 86, 87 -RRB-.
IL-17 also promotes cartilage breakdown by inducing matrix metalloproteinases-1 -LRB- MMP-1 -RRB- from RA synovium -LRB- 86, 87 -RRB-.
Additionally, IL-17 induces cyclooxygenase-2 -LRB- COX-2 -RRB- - dependent prostaglandin E2 -LRB- PGE2 -RRB- synthesis by osteoblasts and it then induces expression of receptor activator of NF-κB ligand -LRB- RANKL -RRB- to differentiate osteoclast progenitors into mature osteoclasts -LRB- 86, 87 -RRB-.
Pro-oxidants such as nitric oxide are also produced by chondrocytes and osteoblasts in response to IL-17 -LRB- 86, 87 -RRB-.
It has been reported that combining inhibitors to block TNF-α and IL-17 has the synergistic effect of suppressing IL-6 production and collagen degradation in the synovium and bone of RA patients -LRB- 89 -RRB-.
More studies will shed light on the validity of anti-IL-17 therapy.
While the role of IL-6 in regulating IL-17 production has only recently been appreciated, the role of IL-6 as a proinflammatory cytokine has long been recognized.
For this reason, targeting IL-6 in RA has been considered for some time.
Indeed the efficacy of humanized anti IL-6R monoclonal antibodies -LRB- tocilizumab/atlizumab -RRB- in the treatment of adults and children with arthritis has recently been reported -LRB- 90 -RRB-.
Also, in April 2008 tocilizumab was been approved in Japan for treatment of RA in Japan, and Phase III trials have been completed in the US -LRB- http://www.clinicaltrials.gov/ -RRB-.
Similarly, in the US, recombinant human anti-IL-1Rα antagonist -LRB- anakinra -RRB- has been approved for use in the treatment of RA -LRB- 91 -RRB-.
Recently, more IL-1-targeting therapies for RA patients are in Phase II studies including anti-IL-1ß monoclonal antibody -LRB- ACZ885 -RRB-, human monoclonal antibody to IL-1R -LRB- AMG108 -RRB-, and IL-1 Trap/rilonacept -LRB- http://www.clinicaltrials.gov/ -RRB-.
On the basis of the efficacy of anti-IL-12p40 therapy in human autoimmune diseases -LRB- 14, 15 -RRB-, a humanized monoclonal anti-IL-12p40 antibody -LRB- ABT-874 -RRB- was tested in RA -LRB- 92 -RRB-.
However this antibody was not shown to be effective because of the trial design -LRB- 92 -RRB-.
Another strategy for targeting IL-12 / IL-23 is apilimod mesylate -LRB- STA-5326 -RRB-, an oral inhibitor of IL-12p35 / p40, which has been tested in a Phase II study for RA -LRB- http://www.clinicaltrials.gov/ -RRB-.
Importantly, the common gamma chain and JAK3 play a pivotal role in the signal transduction of IL-21 -LRB- 25 -RRB-.
In fact, a JAK3 inhibitor -LRB- CP-690550 -RRB- is about to be tested in RA -LRB- Phase II trial -RRB- -LRB- http://www.clinicaltrials.gov/ -RRB-.
Concluding remarks.
The past four years have witnessed major revisions of our views on the lineage commitment of helper T cells.
The conventional Th1/Th2 dichotomy has been replaced by more complex multi-lineage models which do a much better job of explaining the pathogenesis of autoimmunity -LRB- Fig. 1 -RRB-.
However, it is of note that they are also essential for host defense against extracellular bacteria.
Therefore, the challenge will be to keep Th17 function in check to control autoimmunity, while maintaining host defense at the same time.
In this regard, we still need to learn what are the most critical factors for Th17 differentiation.
We also need to better understand which human autoimmune diseases are truly mediated by IL-17 and, by extension, which diseases will benefit most from anti-IL-17 therapy.
With the current pace of investigations on Th17, this field has a great potential for advances.
Estrogen directly activates AID transcription and function.
Abstract.
The immunological targets of estrogen at the molecular, humoral, and cellular level have been well documented, as has estrogen 's role in establishing a gender bias in autoimmunity and cancer.
During a healthy immune response, activation-induced deaminase -LRB- AID -RRB- deaminates cytosines at immunoglobulin -LRB- Ig -RRB- loci, initiating somatic hypermutation -LRB- SHM -RRB- and class switch recombination -LRB- CSR -RRB-.
Furthermore, hyperactivation of AID outside the immune system leads to oncogenesis.
Here, we demonstrate that the estrogen -- estrogen receptor complex binds to the AID promoter, enhancing AID messenger RNA expression, leading to a direct increase in AID protein production and alterations in SHM and CSR at the Ig locus.
Enhanced translocations of the c-myc oncogene showed that the genotoxicity of estrogen via AID production was not limited to the Ig locus.
Outside of the immune system -LRB- e.g., breast and ovaries -RRB-, estrogen induced AID expression by > 20-fold.
The estrogen response was also partially conserved within the DNA deaminase family -LRB- APOBEC3B, -3 F, and -3 G -RRB-, and could be inhibited by tamoxifen, an estrogen antagonist.

Humoral immune responses triggered by foreign antigens require B cell activation.
The activated B cell undergoes antibody affinity maturation, which in higher vertebrates includes somatic hypermutation -LRB- SHM -RRB-, gene conversion of antigen-binding V regions, and class switching -LRB- 1 -RRB- ; all of these processes require activation-induced deaminase -LRB- AID -RRB- -LRB- 2 -- 5 -RRB-.
AID initiates these events by deaminating deoxycytosine to deoxyuracil in DNA -LRB- for review see reference -LSB- 6 -- 8 -RSB- -RRB-.
The resulting dU : dG lesion can be recognized by several different DNA repair pathways to create the aforementioned antibody diversifications.
This necessity for immune diversification and sufficiency for genome instability also highlights AID as an important pathogenic regulator.
In the immune system, hyper - or hypoexpression of AID can alter autoimmune pathologies -LRB- 9 -- 11 -RRB-.
There is strong evidence that AID is required for c-myc translocation, leading to tumorgenesis in a murine model for Burkitt 's lymphoma -LRB- 15, 16 -RRB-.
Other nonphysiological AID targets include BCL6, CD95/Fas, RHO/TTF, PAX-5, and PIM1 -LRB- 12, 17 -- 19 -RRB-.
This gender bias is also reflected in the occurrence of pathogenic immune responses, as found in asthma and other autoimmune diseases -LRB- 28 -- 31 -RRB-.
Several nonimmune pathologies are also strongly influenced by the activity of sex hormones, most notably certain types of cancer.
To further elucidate how AID can be regulated, both within and outside the immune system, and to determine which signaling pathways could use DNA deaminases as DNA instability factors, we analyzed the effect of estrogen on AID 's expression and on downstream pathways such as SHM and class switch recombination -LRB- CSR -RRB-.
We show that AID can be up-regulated by estrogen, whereas tamoxifen -LRB- Tam -RRB- can inhibit this stimulation.
This effect was most pronounced, but not limited to regulation at the level of transcription.
Treatment with estrogen increased AID protein expression, enhanced CSR, augmented mutation frequency in Ig and non-Ig genes, and increased the translocation frequency of c-myc.
Estrogen-induced AID messenger RNA -LRB- mRNA -RRB- production was independent of other B cell stimulatory pathways and could be observed outside immune tissue.
We were able to identify two potential estrogen response elements -LRB- EREs -RRB- near the AID promoter, and determined enhanced ERα binding to the promoter after estrogen treatment in vitro and in vivo.
APOBEC3, the evolutionarily related DNA deaminases -LRB- 34 -RRB-, were also responsive to estrogen treatment in different tissues and cell types.
RESULTS.
Differential effect of sex hormones on AID mRNA.
Hormones such as estrogen and progesterone exert their biological effects through binding to their intracellular receptors and, upon entering the nucleus, act as transcription factors -LRB- 35 -RRB-.
To determine the effects of hormones on AID expression, we stimulated isolated murine splenic B cells with IL-4 and LPS, which are known to induce AID -LRB- 24 -RRB-, while adding physiological amounts of progesterone and estrogen.
Progesterone addition reduced AID mRNA levels by fivefold, as revealed by quantitative real-time PCR -LRB- qRT-PCR ; Fig. 1 A -RRB-.
This and all subsequent qRT-PCR analyses were normalized to GAPDH expression, and all enhancements or repressions were analyzed as relative changes to DMSO.
To observe a stimulatory effect of estrogen, cells were only treated for a short time period -LRB- 8 h -RRB- rather than the usual 24 -- 48 h..
In contrast to progesterone, physiological amounts of estrogen were able to enhance AID expression threefold in these cells -LRB- Fig. 1 A -RRB-.
The effects of estrogen and progesterone on AID mRNA in murine splenic B-cells.
-LRB- A -RRB- AID mRNA in response to estrogen and progesterone treatment in stimulated B cells.
Isolated mouse spleen B cells were stimulated with LPS and IL-4 and treated with different physiological concentrations of estrogen for 8 h or progesterone for 24 h..
Unless indicated, DMSO is set to 1, and treatments are represented as relative change to DMSO.

We focused our subsequent experiments on the verification that the estrogen-induced stimulation on AID was analogous to another known estrogen response gene.
Stimulation of isolated splenic B cells with physiological amounts of estrogen produced a sevenfold increase in AID mRNA -LRB- Fig. 1 B -RRB-.
This induction began to plateau at 4 h, with the earliest indication of an increase detectable at ~ 2 h -LRB- Fig. 1 C -RRB-.
The presence of Tam during the estrogen treatment of isolated splenic B cells inhibited the stimulatory activity, whereas Tam on its own had only a limited effect on AID mRNA expression at the concentration used -LRB- Fig. 1 C, Estrogen 1 nM/Tam and Tam, respectively -RRB-.
Hormonal regulation of AID mRNA is predominantly via transcription.
We pretreated splenic B cells with the translational inhibitor cycloheximide -LRB- CHX -RRB-, followed by stimulation with estrogen, and observed an increase in mRNA production equivalent to treatment without inhibitor -LRB- Fig. S1 B -RRB-.
As estrogen can affect pre-mRNA to mRNA processing -LRB- 38 -RRB-, we designed qRT-PCR primers to span the complete transcription unit of AID -LRB- Fig. S2 A, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-.
When we compared the relative change in expression of the various pre-mRNA 's exons and introns to that of the mature mRNA, we found only a minor effect caused by estrogen treatment -LRB- the 5' - most PCR unit, < 100 bp away from the start of AID gene, was up-regulated to almost the same extent as the mature mRNA -LSB- Fig. S2 B -RSB- -RRB-.
The experiments substantiate the notion that estrogen 's main mode of action on AID is through transcriptional regulation and not mRNA metabolism.
Identification of hormone response elements in the AID promoter regions.
Using bioinformatic analysis -LRB- Fig. 2 A -RRB-, we were able to identify putative EREs in the context of other response elements, such as NF-κB.
We dissected the 1.5 kb upstream and the 2 kb downstream of the ATG regions for hormone-responsive elements in a heterologous transcription assay.
Comparable to the mRNA production of AID in B cells, Fragment C also responded in a dose-dependent manner to estrogen -LRB- Fig. 2 C -RRB-.
Aside from the putative ERE, Fragment C also harbored the two published NF-κB binding sites -LRB- 24 -RRB-.
To more directly stimulate the NF-κB pathway in SiHa cells, we used the cell-autonomous activator TNF-α -LRB- Fig. 2 C -RRB-.
Interestingly, aside from the synergy -LRB- e.g., 10-9 M -RRB-, the two maxima of the dose response were offset -LRB- TNF-γ treated, 10-9 M ; untreated, 10-7 M -RRB-, indicating a higher complexity of the two interacting pathways.
To demonstrate independence of the two pathways, we analyzed the response of Fragment C to treatment with TNF-α and estrogen upon cotransfection of the dominant-negative mutant of IκBα -LRB- IκBα S32A/S36A dominant mutant -LSB- IκBα-mt -RSB- -RRB-, which is known to inhibit the release of NF-κB from the cytoplasm into the nucleus after stimulation.
As shown in Fig. 2 D, the TNF-α activation was inhibited in the presence of IκBα-mt, yet estrogen was able to independently activate the transcription.

ERE binding in B cell extracts.
Thus, we analyzed ER binding to the AID promoter and focused on the more widely expressed receptor subtype ERα.
To analyze the binding of ER to parts of the AID promoter in vitro, we prepared nuclear extracts from treated and untreated cells and performed electromobility shift assays -LRB- EMSA -RRB-.
For the biochemical analysis of the ER binding to the ERE, we focused on NF-κB proximal ERE of Fragment C..
A 34-bp fragment containing the 5' - most proposed ER binding site was incubated with untreated and treated extract -LRB- Fig. 3 B, lanes 2 and 3 -RRB-.
The estrogen treatment clearly induced a protein that could bind the fragment -LRB- arrow -RRB-, which was not induced when treating the B cells with TNF-α before extract preparation -LRB- lane 4 -RRB-.
Competition experiments with the ER binding site -LRB- Fig. 3 B, lanes 6 -- 8 -RRB- or a mutation of the proposed ER site -LRB- Fig. 3 B, lanes 9 -- 11 -RRB- showed a specific competition, indicating ER-like binding kinetics.
Using antibodies to the DNA-binding domain of ERα strongly inhibited the formation of the estrogen-induced band -LRB- Fig. 3 C, lanes 2 vs. 3 -- 5 -RRB-, but the shift was unaffected by a control antibody -LRB- Fig. 3 C, lanes 2 vs. 6 -- 8, arrow -RRB-.

To that end, we probed the published NF-κB site -LRB- 24 -RRB- with our extracts.
Using cold competitors -LRB- Fig. S3 B, lane 4 vs. 6 -- 11, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-, as well as anti -- NF-κB antibodies -LRB- Fig. S3 C -RRB-, we could demonstrate the specificity of the NF-κB binding site.
As with the ER binding site, NF-κB binding was not altered by cotreatment with estrogen and TNF-α -LRB- Fig. S3 B, lanes 4 vs. 5 -RRB-.
Because the distance, on the AID promoter, between the ER and NF-κB sites was larger than our EMSA probes -LRB- i.e., neither probe contained both binding sites -RRB-, we could not study the effect of cooperative binding.
ER binding to AID promoter in vivo.
To this end, we used the constitutive AID-expressing and mutating Burkitt lymphoma Ramos cells and performed chromatin immunoprecipitation -LRB- ChIP -RRB- assay, followed by qRT-PCR.
Treated cells were fixed, lysed, DNA sheared, and ERα or NF-κB immunoprecipitated, and the DNA was released for PCR.
As shown in Fig. 3 D, the anti-ER antibody specifically immunoprecipitated the AID promoter upon estrogen stimulation in a dose-dependent manner.
A control antibody was unable to precipitate this region.
Analogous to the EMSA assay, we did not detect a significant increase in ER binding to AID promoter when we co-stimulated with TNF-α, just as TNF-α treatment alone did not enhance ER binding.
Again, cotreatment of cells with Tam and estrogen before ChIP did reduce the binding of ERα to the AID promoter, whereas Tam on its own did not significantly alter ERα binding -LRB- Fig. 3 D, E 10/Tam and Tam, respectively -RRB-, providing further evidence for a direct binding of ERα to the AID promoter.
Treatment of the cells with TNF-α increased the binding of NF-κB to the AID promoter by more than sevenfold -LRB- Fig. 3 E -RRB-.
Interestingly, co-stimulation of the cells with TNF-α and estrogen had a synergistic effect on the NF-κB binding ; the binding increased to > 30-fold above unstimulated treatment -LRB- 4.5-fold above TNF-α alone -RRB-.
Estrogen up-regulates AID protein production.
We generated a DT40 cell line -LRB- a cell line derived from a chicken B cell lymphoma that constitutively expresses AID and undergoes Ig diversification -RRB- to express a double tag -LRB- 3xFLAG-2xTEV-3xc-Myc -RRB- fused to the C terminal exon of endogenous AID -LRB- AID FLAG-Myc -- tagged AID protein -LSB- AID-FM -RSB- ; Fig. S4, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-.
The modified DT40 express a WT AID protein and an AID-FM fusion protein, both transcribed from the endogenous AID locus.
Comparing the qRT-PCR induction kinetics with that of the AID-FM expression, we determined that the steady-state levels of AID protein correlated to those of the mRNA -LRB- Fig. 4, A and B -RRB-.
Using the translation inhibitor CHX -LRB- Fig. 4 C -RRB-, we showed that estrogen was not able to increase AID-FM expression in the absence of translation.
The aforementioned co-stimulatory effects of TNF-α were also observed at the level of protein production -LRB- Fig. 4, E 10/TNF - α -RRB-.

AID-FM -- tagged DT40 cells were treated with DMSO, 100 nM estrogen, and 10 nM estrogen with TNF-α, lysed, and analyzed for AID mRNA expression with pRT-PCR at various time-points.
-LRB- B -RRB- Estrogen induces AID-FM fusion protein expression.

Hormonal regulation of CSR and SHM.
To analyze CSR, isolated mouse splenic B cells were treated with different combinations of cytokines and hormones.
B cell stimulation with LPS, LPS and IL-4, LPS and IFN-γ, or LPS and TGF-ß results in switching to IgG3, IgG1, IgG2a, or IgG2b/IgA, respectively.
One of the molecular intermediates during class switching is the generation of a looped-out circular DNA called a switch circle -LRB- Fig. S5, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-.
The circular DNA contains a recombined transcription unit that produces switch circle transcripts ; it is generated from the promoter of the downstream switch region and the Igµ switch region.
Using a previously described qRT-PCR approach -LRB- 40 -RRB-, we were able to show enhanced switching to IgG1, IgG3, IgA, or IgE after hormone treatment of splenic B cells -LRB- Fig. 5 A -RRB-.
As with the AID production, this link was perturbed with the addition of Tam during estrogen treatment -LRB- Fig. 5 A, Estrogen 10 nM/Tam and Tam -RRB-.
Hormonal effects on Ig class switching, hypermutation, and translocation.
-LRB- A -RRB- Estrogen induces isotype switching.
Isolated mouse splenic B cells were stimulated for 48 h with LPS + IL-4 for switching to IgG1 and IgE, LPS + TGF-ß for switching to IgA, and LPS for switching to IgG3.
Indicated amounts of estrogen and/or Tam were added to the cells together with cytokines.
Relative efficiency of class switching was determined by detecting circle transcripts with qRT-PCR, and data are normalized to the control treatment with DMSO from three independent experiments -LRB- error bars indicate standard deviations -RRB-.
-LRB- B -RRB- Estrogen increases the mutation frequency in VH and CD95/Fas loci of Ramos, and in Sγ3 of splenic mouse cells.
Ramos cells were grown in the presence of 100 nM estrogen for ~ 20 doublings, followed by sequencing of 341 bp from human VH or 750 bp from human CD95/Fas locus.
Splenic mouse cells were treated for 6 d with LPS and 10 nM estrogen, and switch gamma3 loci amplified and sequenced -LRB- Fig. S7 -RRB-.
Mutation frequencies are normalized to the control treatments with DMSO.
A standard unpaired two-tailed Student 's t test showed a significant difference in mutation frequency in the Sγ3 loci of DMSO - and estrogen-treated spleen cells.
-LRB- C -RRB- Estrogen enhances the c-myc/IgH translocations in splenic B cells from p53 + / - mice.
More than 7 × 107 cells were analyzed by long-range PCR -LRB- 5 × 104 cells/PCR ; Fig. S8 and Supplemental materials and methods -RRB-.
Frequency was determined as c-myc/IgH translocation events per cell number analyzed.
Statistics was performed on the results of the pooled experiments -LRB- two-tailed, unpaired Student 's t test : P = 0.026 -RRB-.
Fig. S7, Fig. S8, and Supplemental materials and methods are available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1.
To determine the effect of estrogen-induced AID on SHM, we sequenced the VH region of in vitro -- cultured Ramos cells, as well as the switch region of γ3 from ex vivo -- stimulated splenic B cells.
A 3-wk estrogen treatment of Ramos HS13 -LRB- 41 -RRB-, which possesses a premature stop codon embedded within the AID target motif WRC, showed enhanced surface Ig expression and VH SHM -LRB- Fig. 5 B and Fig. S6, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-.
Because Ramos expresses constitutive amounts of AID, estrogen treatment did not enhance AID production substantially ; thus, we used the ex vivo treatment of spleens as a means to detect mutations in the switch region -LRB- 42 -RRB-.
To this end, we treated LPS-activated splenic B cells with 10 nM estrogen for 6 d and sequenced the Sγ3 region.
As can be seen in Fig. 5 B and Fig. S7, there was a significant -LRB- P < 0.02 -RRB- enhancement of mutation frequency in the switch region after estrogen treatment.
Enhanced non-Ig loci targeting of AID.
It is known that AID can be mistargeted to non-Ig genes -LRB- 12, 17 -- 19 -RRB-.
CD95/Fas has been shown to be somatically hypermutated in human B cells, albeit 100 -- 1,000-fold less frequently than the Ig genes -LRB- 18 -RRB-.
We analyzed the effects of estrogen on CD95/Fas mutations in Ramos HS13.
Because of the direct effect on AID function -LRB- mutation -RRB-, this data provides evidence for a novel way in which estrogen can exert a direct genotoxic effect on oncogenes or tumor suppressors.
Estrogen enhances c-myc IgH translocations.
The off-target effect of AID was also detected in recent work on chromosome translocations of the c-myc oncogene into the IgH locus.
More importantly, the levels of AID protein directly influenced chromosome translocation frequency.
This was determined from both the analysis of AID haploinsufficiency -LRB- 44 -RRB- and microRNA regulation of AID protein expression -LRB- 45, 46 -RRB-.
In both cases, reduced levels of AID had a direct bearing on the number of observed c-myc/IgH translocations.
Using a previously described assay -LRB- 16, 47 -RRB-, we were able to determine that estrogen treatment of isolated splenic B cells enhances c-myc/IgH translocations in p53 + / - animals -LRB- Fig. 5 C and Fig. S8, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-.
Although, the overall frequency of translocations was low, we have not been able to observe any translocations in LPS/DMSO-treated spleen cells, yet we observed five -LRB- two in one experiment and three in another -RRB- translocations in the LPS/estrogen treatment.
AID induction is not limited to B cells.
Analysis of dissected organs and tissue from mice showed AID responsiveness to hormones outside the immune system in breast and ovarian tissue -LRB- Fig. 6 -RRB-.
As we were primarily interested in the hormone sensitivity of the transcripts, we determined the relative fold stimulation compared with DMSO, which did not reflect the absolute AID mRNA in each tissue.
Interestingly, in ovaries, AID mRNA was induced almost 25-fold, which is higher than in any other organ or tissue.
Estrogen induces AID and Apobec3 transcription in mouse tissue.
The red and blue colors indicate the results for mApobec3 and mAID, respectively.
Tissues were treated with DMSO, 1 nM estrogen -LRB- E1 -RRB-, or 10 nM estrogen -LRB- E10 -RRB-.
Gene expression is normalized to the control treatments with DMSO.
The tissue expression profiles represent pooled data for the respective tissues from two experiments.
Timelines of cell treatments are indicated below the graphs.
Absolute values as compared with GAPDH mRNA are shown in Fig. S10, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1.
Although we did not detect a substantial mRNA increase in hepatocyte or cervix cell lines -LRB- Fig. S9, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-, we were able to show a significant increase -LRB- ranging from 2.5 - to 22-fold -RRB- of AID in cell lines, including T cells, placenta, ovary, breast, and prostate.
The induction observed in breast cells mimics that of the tissues isolated in Fig. 6 A, and confirms a previous report that AID has been detected in the breast cell line MCF-7 -LRB- 48 -RRB-.
Importantly, AID mRNA was not only present at basal levels but was also significantly up-regulated.
Estrogen activates APOBEC3B, 3F, and 3G mRNA transcription.
AID is the ancestral member of the DNA deaminase family, and the APOBEC3 members are considered to have arisen from AID by gene duplication events -LRB- 34 -RRB-.
Within the DNA deaminase family, APOBEC3 members function predominantly in the cytoplasm and inactivate foreign DNA such as retroviruses and retrotransposable elements -LRB- 49 -RRB-.
To this end, we designed qRT-PCR primers to detect APOBEC family member mRNAs in mouse and human cells.
APOBEC2, a related member of the DNA deaminases without any apparent catalytic activity -LRB- 34 -RRB-, was not affected by estrogen treatment ; however, we were able to show that estrogen enhanced transcription of mouse Apobec3 from ovaries, spleen, and splenic B cells -LRB- Fig. 6 -RRB-.
Expression of human APOBEC3B, 3F, and 3G family members was also enhanced upon estrogen treatment from several different cell lines -LRB- including those of T cell, ovarian, placental, and cervical origin ; Fig. S9 -RRB-.
DISCUSSION.
The physiological panpleiotropic effects of hormones are well documented in many aspects of development, although their effector mechanisms at the molecular level, as well as their pathogenic effects upon cancer and immunity are not well understood -LRB- i.e., the gender bias for autoimmunity -LSB- 29, 31, 50 -RSB- is as striking as the gender bias for some cancers -LSB- 51, 52 -RSB- -RRB-.
The correlation between the expression of hormones or their cognitive receptors and development of pathologies, has led to several different hypotheses ; most of which involve hyperactivation of cell proliferation, unregulated differentiation, alteration in DNA repair, or repression of apoptosis -LRB- 51 -RRB-.
Our initial experiment using progesterone and estrogen identified AID as being part of a hormonally regulated system.
Interestingly, AID activation -LRB- mRNA -RRB- by estrogen was more pronounced than the effect on SHM.
Similar to SHM, CSR was enhanced upon estrogen treatment, but was lagging behind AID mRNA production.
The most dramatic effect from estrogen-induced overexpression of AID was seen at the level of c-myc/IgH translocations.
This is analogous to the recent observations that the effect of AID mRNA down-regulation -LRB- either by microRNA targeting or haploinsufficiency -RRB- was most pronounced at the level of translocations -LRB- 44 -- 46 -RRB-.
Autoimmunity encompasses a broadly defined area of clinical pathologies that stem from abnormalities in numerous systemic, cellular, and molecular mechanisms, a subset of which are B cell -- related pathologies -LRB- 50 -RRB-.
In systemic lupus erythematosus, abnormalities in B cell development and the production of autoreactive antibodies play an important pathological role.
Mutation and subsequent loss of growth control is usually associated with oncogenesis, and this similarity with autoimmunity has previously been noted -LRB- 55 -RRB- -LRB- e.g., mutations in CD95/Fas have been associated with autoimmunity, as well as B cell lymphomas -RRB-.
AID 's targeting outside the Ig locus, its apparently crucial involvement with germinal center -- derived B cell malignancies -LRB- 43, 56 -RRB-, and its ability to cause various malignancies when overexpressed in transgenic mice -LRB- 20, 21, 57 -RRB- are strong indicators for AID 's oncogenic potential.
Estrogen is one of the most important and thoroughly studied mitogenic agents in cancer, but it does not possess any direct DNA mutability, and induces transformation by proliferation.
In vitro, high concentrations of estrogen derivatives -LRB- usually metabolites -RRB- can form DNA adducts or produce reactive oxygen-damaging DNA -LRB- for review see reference -LSB- 58 -- 60 -RSB- -RRB-, but their role as physiological genotoxins is limited.
It is interesting to note that the antagonistic activity of Tam has recently been used to inhibit some of the pathologies of estrogen-induced autoimmunity -LRB- 54 -RRB-.
On the other hand, because of the pharmacological action of Tam -LRB- binding and altering the ER DNA binding capacity -RRB-, under certain circumstances Tam acts as an estrogen agonist -LRB- 62 -RRB-.
This activity leads to an increased risk in secondary -LRB- e.g., ovarian -RRB- cancer after Tam treatment for breast cancer -LRB- 63 -RRB-.
It is therefore plausible that the observed estrogen response of AID, as well as its expression in oocytes -LRB- 22 -RRB-, had served a purpose other than targeting AID to Ig genes in B cells.
MATERIALS AND METHODS.
Unless indicated, mouse tissue samples and splenic B cells were derived from 8 -- 12-wk-old female unplugged BALB/c mice, and prepared by standard protocol -LRB- see Supplemental materials and methods, available at available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB-.
Human cell lines Jurkat, T47D, Ramos HS13 -LRB- Ramos -RRB-, JAR, and mouse B cells were cultivated in RPMI-1640 + GlutaMax medium -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB- ; the cell lines MCF7, JAMA2, HeLa, and HepG2 were cultivated in E4 medium ; and PC3 was cultivated in HAMS F12 medium.
Chicken DT40 cells were maintained in RPMI-1640 + GlutaMax with 10 % FCS, 1 % chicken serum, 50 µM ß-mercaptoethanol, 100 U/ml penicillin, and 100 µg / ml streptomycin at 39 ° C with 10 % CO2.
For indicated experiments, cells were treated for 72 h in hormone-depleted serum -LRB- Opti-MeM Reduced Serum Medium ; Invitrogen -RRB- supplemented with Charcoal Stripped Fetal Bovine Serum -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB- ; and nonessential amino acids -LRB- final concentration ; Sigma-Aldrich -RRB-, as follows : l-Alanine -LRB- 8.9 µg / ml -RRB-, l-Asparagine -LRB- 15.0 µg / ml -RRB-, l-Aspartic acid -LRB- 13.3 µg / ml -RRB-, l-Glutamic acid -LRB- 14.7 µg / ml -RRB-, Glycine -LRB- 7.5 µg / ml -RRB-, Proline -LRB- 11.5 µg / ml -RRB-, and l-Serine -LRB- 10.5 µg / ml -RRB-.
B cell stimulation was performed using 25 µg / ml LPS -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB-, 50 ng/ml mouse IL-4 -LRB- R&D Systems -RRB-, 20 ng/ml human TNF-α -LRB- R&D Systems -RRB-, and 2 ng/ml human TGF-ß1 -LRB- R&D Systems -RRB-.
Estrogen -LRB- 17-ß-estradiol ; Sigma-Aldrich -RRB- and progesterone -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB- were dissolved in DMSO at a concentration of 100 mM ; this solution was then diluted in DMSO to give 1,000 × stock solutions, and final dilutions were made in media -LRB- final DMSO concentration was never > 0.1 % -RRB-.
The final concentrations of estrogen are indicated in the text and figure legends.
The concentration of Tam -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB- was 50 nM unless otherwise stated.
The final concentration for CHX -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB- was 10 µg / ml, 20 nM for ACT -LRB- Calbiochem -RRB-, 4 µg / ml for AMA -LRB- Calbiochem -RRB-, and 10 µM for MG-132 -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB-.
qRT-PCR of mRNAs was based on a previous study -LRB- 67 -RRB-, with modifications -LRB- see Supplemental materials and methods -RRB-.
The primers for qRT-PCR -LRB- Table S1, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB- were designed using PrimerExpress software.
qRT-PCR analysis was performed using the QuantiTect SYBR Green PCR kit -LRB- QIAGEN -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's instructions, Abi 7000 Sequence Detection System -LRB- Applied Biosystems -RRB-, and Abi software.
Tissue or cell line hormone responsiveness was determined by qRT-PCR of gene regulated by breast cancer 1, a known estrogen-responsive gene -LRB- 36 -RRB-.
Human AID promoter fragments were analyzed using pE1BLuc plasmid backbone -LRB- provided by G. Akusjärvi, Uppsala University, Uppsala, Sweden -RRB- containing a luciferase ORF and a minimal promoter region.
Primers -LRB- Tables S2 and S3, available at http://www.jem.org/cgi/content/full/jem.20080521/DC1 -RRB- approximately every 500 bp from the human AID transcription start site were used for amplifying AID promoter regions.
The obtained PCR products were cloned into pE1BLuc vector, and 3 µg DNA were transfected into SiHa cells using Lipofectamine 2000 -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's protocols.
24 h after transfection, cells were treated with the indicated concentrations of hormones or TNF-α for 4 h and analyzed thereafter for luciferase signal using Dual Luciferase Reporter Assay System -LRB- Promega -RRB- and Glomax luminometer -LRB- Promega -RRB-.
The expression vector containing a dominant-negative mutant for IκBα -LRB- S32A S36A ; a gift from Felix Randow, Medical Research Council-Laboratory of Molecular Biology, Cambridge, England, UK -RRB- was cotransfected with pE1BLuc constructs where indicated.
1 µg CMV promoter-driven Renilla luciferase expression vector -LRB- Promega -RRB- was included in all transfections and used as an internal control for transfection efficiency.
Ramos cells were treated for 72 h in hormone-depleted serum before the 4-h hormone treatment.
EMSA was performed by standard protocol -LRB- 68 -RRB- with minor modifications -LRB- for more detail see Supplemental materials and methods -RRB-.
Reactions were incubated for 20 min at room temperature in the absence or presence of 1 -, 3 -, and 10-fold mass excess of unlabeled oligonucleotides or antibodies.
Samples were electrophoresed at 4 ° C on 4.5 % polyacrylamide gels for 120 min, followed by autoradiography on imaging plates -LRB- FujiFilm -RRB- and analysis with a FLA-5000 Scanner -LRB- FujiFilm -RRB-.
Ramos cells were treated for 72 h in hormone-depleted serum before the 4-h hormone treatment.
ChIP procedure was done as previously published, with minor modifications -LRB- 69 -RRB- -LRB- for further details see Supplemental materials and methods -RRB-.
Approximately 107 cells were fixed with 1 % formaldehyde in the culture media for 10 min at 37 ° C, and then quenched with 0.125 M glycine for 5 min at RT..
Cells were pelleted and washed twice with cold PBS.
The cell pellet was resuspended in 300 µl SDS lysis buffer and incubated on ice for 10 min.
Cell lysates were sonicated for 6 min with a 30-s on/off sonication cycle in 1.5 ml eppendorf tubes.
Samples were centrifuged for 5 min at 13,000 rpm at 4 ° C, and supernatants were diluted to 1.5 ml with ChIP buffer.
An aliquot was kept as input measurement.
Samples were precleared with 60 µl Protein G beads -LRB- ProtG ; Roche -RRB- and 1 µg salmon sperm DNA -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB- for 45 min at 4 ° C..
Anti -- NF-κB p65 antibody, rabbit anti-ERα HC-20 antibody -LRB- Santa Cruz Biotechnology, Inc. -RRB-, or goat anti -- mouse λ control antibody -LRB- see Supplemental materials and methods -RRB- was added to the supernatant at a concentration of 2 µg / assay and incubated for 12 h at 4 ° C..
