Disruption of DNA binding or CBFß binding abrogates AML1-ETO 's ability to promote self-renewal and inhibit proliferation.
We assessed the importance of DNA binding and heterodimerization with CBFß for AML1-ETO 's ability to confer increased self-renewal capacity to hematopoietic progenitors in vitro .69 -- 71.
Cells expressing AML1-ETO could be propagated for at least 3 weeks in methylcellulose cultures -LRB- Figure 2D -RRB- and yielded primarily immature myeloid lineage cells and a smaller percentage of differentiated macrophages15 ,70 -LRB- not shown -RRB-.
Impaired DNA or CBFß binding caused by the R174Q or Y113A/T161A mutations, respectively, completely abolished AML1-ETO 's ability to sustain this clonogenic activity -LRB- Figure 2D -RRB-.
AML1-ETO inhibits the short-term proliferation of human and mouse primary BM cells .70,71.
The R174Q, T161A, and Y113A/T161A mutations alleviated this repressive effect, although the percentage of cells in S phase was still significantly lower than in MigR1 transduced cells -LRB- Figure 2F, G -RRB-.
CBFß binding is required for AML1-ETO 's leukemogenic activity.
Numerous murine models have demonstrated that full-length AML1-ETO alone is not capable of causing AML .69,72 -- 76.
Activating mutations in the platelet-derived growth factor family of receptor tyrosine kinases, including FLT3 and KIT, and in RAS are common in core binding factor leukemias ,77 -- 81 and correspondingly, AML1-ETO was shown to be capable of cooperating with activated forms of both platelet-derived growth factor receptor-b -LRB- TEL-PDGFßR -RRB- and FLT3 to generate AML in mice .82,83.
We retrovirally transduced AML1-ETO -LRB- and derivative mutants -RRB- and TEL-PDGFßR into BM cells from 5-FU -- treated mice -LRB- Figure 3A -RRB-.
The retrovirus expressing AML1-ETO produced EGFP from an internal ribosome entry site, and the TEL-PDGFßR virus produced hCD4.
The percentages of doubly transduced cells -LRB- EGFP + hCD4 + -RRB- were similar for AML1-ETO and various mutants thereof at 2 days after spinfection -LRB- Figure 3B -RRB-.
We transplanted lethally irradiated primary recipient animals with 106 retrovirally transduced, unsorted cells and monitored the animals for disease.
The AML that develops in mice transplanted with BM cells expressing both AML1-ETO and TEL-PDGFßR is marked clinically by splenomegaly, hepatomegaly, thrombocytopenia, and anemia with an accumulation of myeloid blasts in the BM and an infiltration thereof in the spleen and liver .82.
TEL-PDGFßR will independently generate a chronic myeloproliferative disorder -LRB- CMPD -RRB- marked by splenomegaly, hepatomegaly, and neutrophilic leukocytosis .84.
Mutations that disrupt DNA or CBFß binding impair AML1-ETO 's leukemogenic activity.
-LRB- A -RRB- Schematic of transplantation scheme.
BM mononuclear cells harvested from 5-FU -- treated C57BL/6 mice were co-infected with MigR1 expressing AML1-ETO -LRB- and its mutated derivatives -RRB- and TEL-PDGFßR.
Internal ribosome entry site -LRB- IRES -RRB- -- mediated expression of EGFP marks AML1-ETO expressing cells, while hCD4 marks TEL-PDGFßR expressing cells.
Retrovirally transduced cells -LRB- 106 -RRB- were transplanted along with 2 × 105 normal BM cells into lethally irradiated mice.
-LRB- B -RRB- FACS plots of BM cells 2 days after transduction to show that all were equivalently infected.
-LRB- C -RRB- Kaplan-Meier survival curve of mice after transplantation with retroviruses expressing AML1-ETO -LRB- AE -RRB- or its mutated derivatives and TEL-PDGFßR -LRB- TP -RRB-.
The study end point was 63 days.
The number of mice in each group is indicated.
-LRB- D -RRB- Spleen weights of mice upon sacrifice.
Significant differences from AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR recipients -LRB- # -RRB- are indicated with * -LRB- Dunnett test and ANOVA -RRB-.
-LRB- E -RRB- Representative plots of BM cells in transplant recipients upon sacrifice demonstrating the presence of EGFP + and hCD4 + cells.
The relatively high EGFP fluorescence in the AML1-ETO -LRB- Y113A/T161A -RRB- plus TEL-PDGFßR BM cells was observed in 19 of 24 mice.
-LRB- F -RRB- Average percentage of EGFP - hCD4 + and EGFP + hCD4 + BM cells in transplant recipients upon sacrifice.
Error bars indicate 95 % confidence intervals.
Differences relative to AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR -LRB- # -RRB- for each group were determined using Dunnett test and ANOVA.
-LRB- G -RRB- Cytospin preparations of BM cells from an AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR leukemic mouse purified based on hCD4 and EGFP expression.
Mice transplanted with BM cells expressing both AML1-ETO and TEL-PDGFßR developed a completely penetrant lethal leukemia, as reported previously ,82 and succumbed to their disease within 4 weeks -LRB- Figure 3C -RRB-.
In contrast, most control mice transplanted with cells expressing AML1-ETO alone -LRB- 8/8 -RRB-, or TEL-PDGFßR alone -LRB- 7/8 -RRB- survived for 63 days, at which point they were killed for analysis.
Diseased AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR transplanted mice presented with anemia, splenomegaly, and pale livers -LRB- not shown -RRB-.
Their BM contained blast cells characterized by a high nucleocytoplasmic ratio, heterochromatic nuclei, occasional cytoplasmic vacuoles, irregular nuclear contours, and prominent nucleoli -LRB- not shown -RRB-.
Blast cells were also present in peripheral blood -LRB- not shown -RRB-.
As a result of the mixed diseases in these mice, BM differentials and histology were not useful diagnostic aids.
We therefore isolated EGFP-hCD4 + and EGFP + hCD4 + cells from the BM of leukemic AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR mice and analyzed their morphology.
The EGFP + hCD4 + population -LRB- expressing AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR -RRB- contained a markedly greater percentage of blast cells, consistent with AML, in comparison to the EGFP-hCD4 + population -LRB- Figure 3G -RRB-.
Most mice transplanted with BM expressing TEL-PDGFßR plus either the non-DNA binding or non-CBFß binding AML1-ETO mutants -LRB- R174Q and Y113A/T161A, respectively -RRB- survived until the study end point of 63 days -LRB- Figure 3C -RRB-.
The majority of these mice had evidence of disease as manifested by enlarged spleens -LSB- 15/22 for AML1-ETO -LRB- R174Q -RRB- and 22/24 for AML1-ETO -LRB- Y113A/T161A -RRB- -RSB-.
A minority of the mice were anemic as evidenced by pale livers -LSB- 2/22 for AML1-ETO -LRB- R174Q -RRB- and 6/24 for AML1-ETO -LRB- Y113A/T161A -RRB- -RSB-, whereas anemia was more prevalent in the AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR mice -LRB- 16/22 -RRB-.
Despite having more EGFP + hCD4 + cells and higher AML1-ETO levels, the AML1-ETO -LRB- Y113A/T161A -RRB- plus TEL-PDGFßR group survived longer than the AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR group, thus AML1-ETO deficient for CBFß binding has greatly attenuated activity.
We were unable to detect AML1-ETO protein in spleen samples from any of the transplanted mice using antibodies that recognize either ETO or the Runt domain from Runx1, although we could detect the protein in Kasumi-1 cells which contain the t -LRB- 8 ; 21 -RRB-, and actin was clearly visible in all of the samples -LRB- not shown -RRB-.
EGFP + hCD4 + BM cells -LRB- expressing AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR -RRB- from the AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR recipients contained significantly higher percentages of c-kit + Sca-1 + cells than those expressing either of the mutated AML1-ETO proteins or TEL-PDGFßR alone -LRB- Figure 4A, B -RRB-.
The percentage of Gr1 + Mac1 + cells in the EGFP + hCD4 + BM population was correspondingly lower in the AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR group than in any other, reflective of impaired granulocyte differentiation -LRB- Figure 4A, C -RRB-.
Flow cytometric analysis of BM from primary transplant recipients.
-LRB- A -RRB- Whole BM of diseased mice was gated based on forward and side scatter characteristics and subsequently analyzed for expression of hCD4 -LRB- TEL-PDGFßR -RRB- and EGFP -LRB- AML1-ETO -RRB-.
EGFP + hCD4 + cells were then analyzed for the expression of myeloid and progenitor markers.
Plots are from a single animal that is representative of the experimental group.
-LRB- B -RRB- Differences in the percentage of EGFP + hCD4 + BM cells that were positive for both c-kit and Sca-1.

Differences relative to AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR -LRB- # -RRB- for each group were determined using Dunnett test and ANOVA.
-LRB- C -RRB- Differences in the percentage of EGFP + hCD4 + BM cells that were positive for both Gr-1 and Mac-1.
Error bars indicate 95 % confidence intervals.
Differences relative to AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR -LRB- # -RRB- for each group were determined using Dunnett test and ANOVA.
The percentage of Gr-1 + Mac-1 + cells in mice transplanted with AML1-ETO -LRB- Y113A/T161A -RRB- plus TEL-PDGFßR transduced cells was significantly lower -LRB- P < .001 -RRB- than in mice transplanted with BM expressing AML1-ETO -LRB- R174Q -RRB- plus TEL-PDGFßR or TEL-PDGFßR alone.
In summary, cells expressing AML1-ETO plus TEL-PDGFßR gave rise to a rapid AML as reported previously .82.
Mutations in AML1-ETO that impaired DNA binding significantly weakened its activity, resulting in an extended latency and disease specificity more closely resembling that caused by TEL-PDGFßR alone.
Loss of CBFß binding also weakened AML1-ETO 's activity, resulting in an extended disease latency, selection of higher AML1-ETO expressing cells, and a cell surface phenotype intermediate between AML and CMPD.
Disruption of CBFß binding by the Runt domain of TEL-AML1 abrogates its ability to enhance self-renewal of B-cell progenitors.
TEL-AML1 is critically dependent upon DNA binding to enhance the self-renewal of B-cell progenitors in culture .61.
We transduced c-Kit + fetal liver cells from embryonic day 12 C57BL/6 mice with retroviruses expressing TEL-AML1 or its mutated derivatives and EGFP ,61,66 and serially replated them in methylcellulose under conditions that promote B-cell differentiation.
Expression of similar steady-state levels of the TEL-AML1 mutant proteins in transduced NIH3T3 cells was confirmed by Western blot analysis, and retroviral transduction of c-kit + cells was measured by EGFP fluorescence -LRB- Figure 5A, B -RRB-.
Cells expressing TEL-AML1 generated increased numbers of colonies and cells, which are B220 enriched, more than multiple rounds of replating relative to cells expressing EGFP alone -LRB- Figure 5C-E -RRB-.
A reduction in CBFß heterodimerization by greater than 400-fold through introduction of the Y140A/T188A mutations severely impaired TEL-AML1 's ability to enhance the clonogenic potential of these B-cell precursors, as the numbers of cells and colonies were very similar to those of EGFP-transduced cells.
Cells expressing the T188A TEL-AML1 mutant, which is expected to have an approximately 60-fold reduction in CBFß binding, produced numbers of colonies and cells similar to those of TEL-AML1 -- expressing cells during secondary replating, however, the numbers from the third round of replating were very significantly decreased and therefore somewhat intermediate between the TEL-AML1 and TEL-AML1 -LRB- Y140A/T188A -RRB- expressing cells.
As the thermodynamic stability and DNA binding affinity of the T118A and Y140A/T188A mutant Runt domains are identical, the decreased activity can only be explained by more severely impaired CBFß binding.
Disrupting heterodimerization with CBFß substantially abrogates TEL-AML1 's ability to enhance the clonogenic potential of c-kit + B-cell precursors.
-LRB- A -RRB- Detection of hemagglutinin -LRB- HA -RRB- -- tagged TEL-AML1 and the T188A and Y140A/T188A mutants in NIH3T3 cells 48 hours after retroviral -LRB- murine stem cell virus -LSB- MSCV -RSB- -RRB- transduction.
Vertical lines have been inserted to indicate a repositioned gel lane.
-LRB- B -RRB- Flow cytometric analysis of EGFP expression in c-kit + fetal liver cells 48 hours after infection with viral supernatants.
-LRB- C -RRB- Transduced c-kit + cells grown in methylcellulose serial replating assays in conditions promoting B-cell differentiation -LRB- IL-7, SCF, and FLT3 ligand -RRB-.
The number of colonies harvested from each culture, per 104 cells plated, is shown for the first -LRB- -RRB-, second -LRB- -RRB-, and third -LRB- ¦ -RRB- rounds of plating.
Plots show means and SDs of duplicate cultures.
The data shown are representative of 5 independent experiments.
-LRB- D -RRB- Total number of cells, as in panel C. -LRB- E -RRB- Number of B220 + cells as in panel C..
Discussion.
Assessing which protein-protein interactions mediated by oncogenic transcription factors are essential for their leukemogenic activity, and determining the structures of the domains responsible for those interactions will greatly facilitate the development of specific inhibitors by structure-aided drug design.
Here, we show that ablation of DNA binding by 40000 fold30 ,49 or reduction of CBFß heterodimerization by greater than 400-fold partially impaired AML1-ETO 's ability to inhibit granulocyte differentiation, almost completely reversed its acute inhibition of proliferation, eliminated its ability to confer serial replating to myeloid progenitors, and severely compromised its cooperation with TEL-PDGFßR to cause AML, and thus impaired or delayed AML disease.
Similarly, inhibition of both DNA61 and CBFß binding by TEL-AML1 eliminated its ability to enhance the self-renewal of B-cell progenitors.
Although small molecules targeting protein-protein interactions are relatively limited thus far, there has been an increase in activity and reported success in developing these inhibitors .85.
For example, we recently developed a small molecule that binds CBFß and allosterically inhibits CBFß binding to the Runt domain, supporting the notion that disrupting this interaction with drug-like molecules is feasible .86.
Although CBFß is clearly important for AML1-ETO and TEL-AML1 function, the nature of its activity is not completely understood.
It has long been known that CBFß increases the Runx proteins' affinity for DNA ,88,89 and it was more recently shown that it protects them from ubiquitin-mediated proteolysis .37,90.
However, genetic data in both flies and worms hint at other functions.
More recently, it was shown that ectopic overexpression of CBFß -LRB- BRO-1 -RRB- could partially restore a Runx -LRB- RNT -RRB- -- deficient defect in Caenorhabditis elegans .92.
Although repression of granulocyte differentiation is a consistent feature of AML1-ETO overexpression ,15,25,70,73,75 it is not entirely clear how important it is to AML1-ETO 's leukemogenic function.
We found several AML1-ETO mutants that were able to partially repress granulocyte differentiation but had no leukemogenic activity, nor was a granulocyte differentiation defect observed in a conditional AML1-ETO knock-in model .69.
What is clear, however, from our data and that of Yan et al ,49 is that DNA binding by AML1-ETO is essential for its leukemogenic activity and that this observation must be incorporated into any mechanistic model for AML1-ETO function.
O-Linked N-Acetylglucosaminylation of Sp1 Inhibits the Human Immunodeficiency Virus Type 1 Promoter.
Abstract.
Human immunodeficiency virus type 1 -LRB- HIV-1 -RRB- gene expression and replication are regulated by the promoter/enhancer located in the U3 region of the proviral 5' long terminal repeat -LRB- LTR -RRB-.
The binding of cellular transcription factors to specific regulatory sites in the 5' LTR is a key event in the replication cycle of HIV-1.
In the present study we demonstrate that treatment of HIV-1-infected lymphocytes with the O-GlcNAcylation-enhancing agent glucosamine -LRB- GlcN -RRB- repressed viral transcription in a dose-dependent manner.
Overexpression of O-GlcNAc transferase -LRB- OGT -RRB-, the sole known enzyme catalyzing the addition of O-GlcNAc to proteins, specifically inhibited the activity of the HIV-1 LTR promoter in different T-cell lines and in primary CD4 + T lymphocytes.
Inhibition of HIV-1 LTR activity in infected T cells was most efficient -LRB- > 95 % -RRB- when OGT was recombinantly overexpressed prior to infection.
O-GlcNAcylation of the transcription factor Sp1 and the presence of Sp1-binding sites in the LTR were found to be crucial for this inhibitory effect.
From this study, we conclude that O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 inhibits the activity of the HIV-1 LTR promoter.

Human immunodeficiency virus type 1 -LRB- HIV-1 -RRB- gene expression is regulated by the long terminal repeat -LRB- LTR -RRB- promoter, which is composed of three regions : U3 -LRB- unique 3' end -RRB-, R -LRB- repeated -RRB-, and U5 -LRB- unique 5' end -RRB-.
The U3 region contains an upstream regulatory element including binding sites for several cellular transcription factors such as the nuclear factor of activated T cells 1 -LRB- NFATc1 -RRB- and the activator protein 1 -LRB- AP-1 -RRB-, an enhancer with two binding sites for the nuclear factor κB -LRB- NF-κB -RRB-, and the core promoter composed of three tandem binding sites for specificity protein 1 -LRB- Sp1 -RRB- and a TATA box.
While NF-κB is a strong enhancer of HIV-1 transcription -LRB- 8 -RRB-, Sp1 is essential for basal transcription and Tat-mediated activation of HIV-1 -LRB- 25, 69 -RRB-.
This is concordant with the fact that Sp1 is upregulated in activated T cells -LRB- 43 -RRB-, which compose the primary reservoir for HIV-1 replication -LRB- 68 -RRB-.
Importantly, deletion of all three Sp1-binding sites reduces viral replication in human T-cell cultures -LRB- 58 -RRB-.
In eukaryotic cells, myriad cytoplasmic and nuclear proteins are posttranslationally modified at the hydroxyl groups of specific serine and threonine residues by a single monosaccharide, N-acetyl-d-glucosamine -LRB- GlcNAc -RRB- -LRB- 26, 80 -RRB-.
The O-glycosidic linkage of GlcNAc to proteins is a highly dynamic and reversible posttranslational modification and differs from other glycosylation events in that it occurs in the cytosol and the nucleus rather than in the Golgi apparatus or the endoplasmic reticulum.
Protein O-linked N-acetyl-d-glucosaminylation -LRB- O-GlcNAcylation -RRB- is catalyzed by O-GlcNAc transferase -LRB- OGT -RRB- and reversed by O-GlcNAc hexosaminidase -LRB- O-GlcNAcase -RRB- -LRB- 30 -RRB-.
The substrate for protein O-GlcNAcylation is UDP-GlcNAc.
Therefore, O - GlcNAcylation is regulated by the cellular levels of OGT and O-GlcNAcase and by the availability of UDP-GlcNAc -LRB- 81 -RRB-.
As UDP-GlcNAc is synthesized de novo from glucose via the hexosamine biosynthetic pathway, glucose flux through the hexosamine biosynthetic pathway increases O-GlcNAcylation of proteins.
Furthermore, compounds like glucosamine -LRB- GlcN -RRB-, streptozotocin, O - -LRB- 2-acetamido-2-deoxy-d-glucopyranosylidene -RRB- amino-N-phenylcarbamate -LRB- PUGNAc -RRB-, and 2-deoxyglucose enhance O-GlcNAcylation of proteins either by increasing the availability of UDP-GlcNAc or by inhibiting the enzyme O-GlcNAcase -LRB- 23, 37, 63 -RRB-.
Protein O-GlcNAcylation has been shown to modulate -LRB- i -RRB- enzyme activity, -LRB- ii -RRB- protein-protein interactions, -LRB- iii -RRB- DNA-binding affinity, -LRB- iv -RRB- subcellular localization, and -LRB- v -RRB- the half-life and proteolytic processing of proteins -LRB- 81 -RRB-.
Furthermore, O-GlcNAcylation often plays an antagonistic role in relation to phosphorylation -LRB- 36 -RRB-.
Furthermore, O-GlcNAc plays a pivotal role in the regulation of gene expression via modification of RNA polymerase II -LRB- 12, 39 -RRB- and associated transcription factors -LRB- 31, 32 -RRB-.
Thus, O-GlcNAc serves as a nutrient sensor to couple the metabolic status to cellular processes, such as protein degradation, signal transduction, and gene transcription.
Some of the transcription factors involved in HIV-1 gene regulation are modified by O-GlcNAc, including AP-1 -LRB- 67 -RRB-, yin-yang 1 -LRB- YY1 -RRB- -LRB- 28 -RRB-, NFATc1 -LRB- 21 -RRB-, NF-κB -LRB- 21 -RRB-, and Sp1 -LRB- 31, 62 -RRB-.
Sp1 was the first transcription factor identified as being O-GlcNAcylated -LRB- 31 -RRB-.
Sp1 is ubiquitous and belongs to the Sp1-like/Kr üppel-like family of transcription factors characterized by three C-terminal Cys2His2 zinc finger motifs -LRB- 34 -RRB- and a DNA-binding affinity to GC-rich sites -LRB- 16 -RRB-.
Two decades ago, Tjian and coworkers showed that Sp1 bears at least eight O-GlcNAc sites and that the O-GlcNAcylated form of Sp1 was more active than the non-O-GlcNAcylated protein -LRB- 31 -RRB-.
Since Sp1 is critical and important for HIV-1 transcription -LRB- 25 -RRB- and Sp1 activity is modulated by O-GlcNAc -LRB- 42 -RRB-, we investigated the effect of Sp1 O-GlcNAcylation on the activity of the HIV-1 LTR promoter.
Here we show that an increased O-GlcNAc level represses the HIV-1 LTR promoter activity.
This required O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 and the presence of Sp1-binding sites in the HIV-1 LTR.
MATERIALS AND METHODS.
Jurkat and T1 -LRB- 174 × CEM.T1 -RRB- cells were maintained in very-low-endotoxin-Roswell Park Memorial Institute -LRB- RPMI -RRB- 1640 medium -LRB- Biochrom, Berlin, Germany -RRB- supplemented with 10 % fetal calf serum -LRB- FCS ; Biochrom -RRB- and 2 mM l-glutamine -LRB- PAA, Cölbe, Germany -RRB- at 37 ° C in a humidified atmosphere at 5 % CO2.
CD4 + T cells were isolated using anti-CD4 magnetically activated cell sorting beads -LRB- Miltenyi, Bergisch Gladbach, Germany -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's instructions.
CD4 + T cells were cultured in MLPC medium consisting of RPMI 1640, 10 % human serum, 2 mM l-glutamine, 20 mg/liter gentamicin, 10 mM HEPES, 1 mM sodium pyruvate, and 1 % minimum essential medium nonessential amino acids -LRB- all from PAA, Cölbe, Germany -RRB- at 37 ° C under 5 % CO2.
HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells were obtained through the AIDS Research and Reference Reagent Program, Division of AIDS, NIAID, NIH, from Masahiko Satoh -LRB- 57 -RRB-.
These cells stably express d1EGFP -LRB- which was derived from d2EGFP, a destabilized, redshifted variant of the enhanced green fluorescent protein -LSB- EGFP -RSB-, and has a half-life of approximately 1 hour -RRB- under the control of the HIV-1 LTR promoter.
HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells were cultivated in Dulbecco 's modified Eagle 's medium -LRB- PAA -RRB- supplemented with 10 % FCS, 2 mM l-glutamine, and 1 mg/ml G418 at 37 ° C under 8.5 % CO2.
HEK 293T cells were cultivated in Dulbecco 's modified Eagle 's medium supplemented with 10 % FCS and 2 mM l-glutamine at 37 ° C under 8.5 % CO2.
Pseudoviruses were produced by cotransfection of HEK 293T cells with pNL4-3LucR-E - -LRB- obtained through the AIDS Research and Reference Reagent Program, Division of AIDS, NIAID, NIH, from Nathaniel Landau -LSB- 13, 27 -RSB- -RRB- and a vesicular stomatitis virus G protein -LRB- VSV-G -RRB- - encoding plasmid by using the calcium phosphate technique.
Pseudovirus-containing supernatants were harvested 2 days after transfection, and cellular debris was removed by centrifugation at 300 × g for 5 min.
HIV-1 p24 concentration was estimated by antigen enzyme-linked immunosorbent assay.
Pseudovirus-containing supernatants were stored in 1-ml aliquots at -80 ° C until use.
Jurkat and T1 cells were cultured to a density of 1.5 × 106 cells/ml and split 1:2 on the day prior to infection.
Cells were infected with VSV-G env pseudotyped HIV-1NL4-3LucR-E - for 4 h at 37 ° C, using a concentration of 30 ng p24 per 1 × 106 cells.
Cells were centrifuged at 300 × g for 5 min to remove excessive pseudovirus and resuspended in 2 ml very-low-endotoxin-RPMI 1640 containing 2 mM l-glutamine and 10 % FCS supplemented with the respective concentration of GlcN -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich, Munich, Germany -RRB- in triplicate.
CD4 + T cells were stimulated for 6 days with 10 U/ml interleukin-2 -LRB- Roche, Mannheim, Germany -RRB- and 10 µg / ml phytohemagglutinin P -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB- prior to infection.
Cells were infected with reporter HIV-1 for 4 h at 37 ° C, using a concentration of 30 ng p24 per 2 × 106 cells.
Cells were centrifuged at 250 × g for 10 min to remove excessive pseudovirus and resuspended in 1.5 ml MLPC medium supplemented with the respective concentration of GlcN in triplicate.
After incubation for 24 h, cells were collected, washed once with phosphate-buffered saline -LRB- PBS ; Biochrom -RRB-, lysed in 1 × passive lysis buffer -LRB- Promega, Mannheim, Germany -RRB-, and assayed for luciferase activity as described below.
Cell viability was measured using the CellTiter 96 nonradioactive cell proliferation assay -LRB- MTT -LSB- 3 - -LRB- 4,5-dimethyl-2-thiazolyl -RRB- -2,5 - diphenyl-2H-tetrazolium bromide -RSB- assay ; Promega -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's protocol.
Briefly, 100-µl cell suspensions containing either 1 × 105 HIV-1-infected Jurkat or T1 cells or 2 × 105 HIV-1-infected CD4 + primary T lymphocytes were applied for the assay.
The coding sequence of OGT was cloned by amplifying 820 bp corresponding to the N terminus of nucleocytoplasmic OGT, GenBank accession number NM_181672 -LRB- 24, 41 -RRB-, from human cDNA with specific primers containing the restriction sites for BamHI and EcoRV -LRB- underlined -RRB- and a Kozak sequence -LRB- italics -RRB- -LRB- forward primer, 5' - TAGGGATCCGATATCGCCACCATGGCGTCTTCCGTGGGCAACG-3' -RRB- and the restriction site for StuI -LRB- underlined -RRB- -LRB- reverse primer, 5' - AGATCTATCAGGCCTTGCTCATAG-3' -RRB-.
The PCR fragment was then ligated with the StuI restriction site to the part of the Lv4F fragment -LRB- also termed mitochondrial OGT ; GenBank accession number U77413 -LSB- 46, 47 -RSB- -RRB- which corresponds to the C terminus of nucleocytoplasmic OGT and harbors a NotI restriction site at the 3' end.
The complete sequence for the human nucleocytoplasmic OGT was subsequently inserted into pcDNA4/myc-His B -LRB- Invitrogen, Karlsruhe, Germany -RRB- at the EcoRV and NotI sites.
The rescue mutant resOGT was created by mutagenesis PCR using pcDNA-OGT as template and the QuikChange XL site-directed mutagenesis kit -LRB- Stratagene, Amsterdam, The Netherlands -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's instructions.
The mutagenic primers were designed by the QuikChange primer design program : forward primer, 5' - GAGGCACGGCAACCTGTGCTTAGATAAGATCAACGTGCTGCACAAGCCACCATATGAACATCCAAAAGA-3' ; reverse primer, 5' - TCTTTTGGATGTTCATATGGTGGCTTGTGCAGCACGTTGATCTTATCTAAGCACAGGTTGCCGTGCCTC-3' -LRB- nucleotide changes compared to the wild-type sequence are in bold -RRB-.
The expression plasmid for Sp1 was generated by subcloning the XbaI/SmaI fragment of the pBS-Sp1-f1 vector -LRB- GenBank accession number AF252284 -LSB- 35 -RSB- -RRB-, representing the open reading frame of Sp1, into the XbaI/EcoRV-digested pcDNA3 .1 -LRB- - -RRB- vector -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB-.
The reporter constructs pXP1-LTR-κB-Sp1wt-Luc, pXP1-LTR-κB-Sp1mut-Luc, and pXP1-LTR-Sp1wt-Luc were kindly provided by Manuel López-Cabrera -LRB- 2, 22 -RRB-.
The plasmid pcDNA4-LTRwt-d2EGFP -LRB- destabilized, redshifted variant of the EGFP with a half-life of approximately 2 hours -RRB- was cloned by insertion of d2EGFP into pcDNA4/myc-His B plasmid -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB- via XhoI and XbaI.
HIV-1 wild-type LTR -LRB- LTRwt -RRB- was amplified from pNL4-3, obtained through the AIDS Research and Reference Reagent Program, Division of AIDS, NIAID, NIH, from Malcolm Martin -LRB- 1 -RRB-, using the following primers : forward primer, 5' - GACAATTGAAGAAAAGGGGGGACTGGAAGGGCTAATTCACTC-3' ; reverse primer, 5' - ACCTCGAGTTGGCTCACTGCAACCTCTACCTCCTGGGTGCT-3'.
The amplified LTRwt DNA was digested with MfeI and XhoI -LRB- underlined -RRB- and ligated into pcDNA4-d2EGFP.
The plasmid pcDNA4-LTRmutSp1-d2EGFP contained the Sp1-binding-site-mutated LTR -LRB- LTRmutSp1 -RRB- and was created by QuikChange XL site-directed mutagenesis PCR using the forward primer 5' - GGGGACTTTCCAGGGATTCGTGGCCTGTTCGGGACTGGTTAGTGGCGA-3' and the reverse primer 5' - CTCGCCACTAACCAGTCCCGAACAGGCCACGAATCCCTGGAAAGTCCCC-3' -LRB- nucleotide changes compared to the wild-type sequence are in bold -RRB-.
The Tat expression construct pCEP4-Tat was obtained through the AIDS Research and Reference Reagent Program, Division of AIDS, NIAID, NIH, from Lung-Ji Chang -LRB- 9 -RRB-.
The control reporter plasmid pEF1α-Luc was constructed by subcloning the elongation factor 1 alpha -LRB- EF1α -RRB- promoter from pEF1/Myc-His vector -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB- into the promoterless pGL3-Basic vector -LRB- Promega -RRB-.
pcDNA4-EF1α-d2EGFP was generated by replacing the cytomegalovirus promoter in the plasmid pcDNA4-d2EGFP with the EF1α promoter.
All cloned constructs were confirmed by full-length sequencing and expression experiments.
The plasmid pGEM4Z-OGT-64A was generated by subcloning the OGT gene from pcDNA4-OGT into the RNA production vector pGEM4Z-5 ` UTR-sig-huSurvivin-DC. LAMP-3 ` UTR-64A -LRB- kindly provided by Kris Thielemans -LSB- 4 -RSB- -RRB-, replacing the huSurvivin-DC. LAMP.
The pGEM4Z-EGFP-64A vector was provided by I..
Tcherepanova, Argos Therapeutics, Durham, NC -LRB- 66 -RRB-.
The constructs were confirmed by restriction digest and expression experiments.
HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells were treated with the respective GlcN concentrations for 5 h in triplicate.
HEK 293T-LTRwt-d2EGFP and HEK 293T-LTRmutSp1-d2EGFP cells were treated with 16 mM GlcN for 20 h in duplicate.
The cells were harvested with trypsin-EDTA -LRB- PAA -RRB-, washed twice with FACS-PBS -LRB- PBS containing 5 % FCS and 0.1 % sodium azide -LSB- Sigma-Aldrich -RSB- -RRB- and resuspended in FACS-PBS.
Viable GFP-positive cells -LRB- 1 × 104 -RRB- were analyzed for each sample using a FACSCalibur flow cytometer with CellQuest Pro software -LRB- both from BD Biosciences, Heidelberg, Germany -RRB-.
The relative fluorescence intensity is given as a ratio of the geometric mean of untreated cells to that of GlcN-treated cells.
The geometric mean of untreated cells was defined as 100 %.
In vitro transcription of RNA was performed as described previously -LRB- 65 -RRB-.
In short, the pGEM4Z-OGT-64A and pGEM4Z-EGFP-64A vectors were linearized with NotI and SpeI enzyme, respectively, purified by phenol-chloroform extraction and ethanol precipitation, and used as DNA templates.
The in vitro transcription was performed with T7 RNA polymerase -LRB- mMessage mMachine T7 Ultra kit ; Ambion/Applied Biosystems, Austin, TX -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's instructions.
After DNase I -LRB- Ambion -RRB- digestion and poly -LRB- A -RRB- tailing -LRB- Ambion -RRB-, the transcribed RNA was recovered on RNeasy columns -LRB- Qiagen GmbH, Hilden, Germany -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's instructions.
RNA quality was verified by agarose gel electrophoresis, and the RNA concentration was measured spectrophotometrically.
The protein concentration was determined in a microplate reader model 680 -LRB- Bio-Rad, Munich, Germany -RRB- at 750 nm using a detergent-compatible -LRB- DC -RRB- protein assay kit -LRB- Bio-Rad -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's protocol.
Cells were lysed as described under `` Cell transfection '' and `` HIV-1 infection and GlcN treatment. ''.
Samples were prepared in 6 × sodium dodecyl sulfate -LRB- SDS -RRB- buffer -LRB- 350 mM Tris-HCl, pH 6.8, 30 % glycerol, 10 % SDS, 0.6 M dithiothreitol, 0.012 % bromophenol blue -RRB-, boiled for 10 min at 99 ° C, and loaded on 7.5 % acrylamide-bisacrylamide gels or 4 to 20 % Tris-glycine gradient gels -LRB- Anamed, Gross-Bieberau, Germany -RRB-.
Gel-separated proteins were transferred to a polyvinylidene fluoride membrane -LRB- Roth, Karlsruhe, Germany -RRB-, which was blocked with 5 % nonfat dry milk in PBS-Tween -LRB- PBS containing 0.1 % Tween 20 -RRB- for 2 h, washed with PBS-Tween, and incubated with the primary antibody in 2.5 % nonfat dry milk in PBS-Tween at room temperature for 2 h..
After washing, the membranes were incubated for 45 min at room temperature with the secondary antibody in 2.5 % nonfat dry milk in PBS-Tween -LRB- 71, 76 -RRB-.
In order to prevent cross-reactions with milk proteins, Western blot staining with the O-GlcNAc-recognizing antibody was performed as follows : the membranes were blocked with 10 % Western blocking reagent -LRB- Roche -RRB- in PBS-Tween and the antibody was diluted in 0.5 % Western blocking reagent -LRB- Roche -RRB-.
Subsequent to the final washing step, chemiluminescence was detected according to the manufacturer 's protocol -LRB- Pierce Biotechnology, Rockford, IL -RRB-.
The following primary antibodies were used : polyclonal rabbit anti-human Sp1 Pep2 -LRB- 1:500 ; Santa Cruz Biotechnology, Heidelberg, Germany -RRB-, polyclonal goat anti-human lamin A/C N-18 -LRB- 1:1,000 ; Santa Cruz Biotechnology -RRB-, polyclonal rabbit anti-human OGT TI-14 -LRB- 1:1,000 ; Sigma-Aldrich -RRB-, polyclonal rabbit anti-human actin -LRB- 1:1,000 ; Sigma-Aldrich -RRB-, monoclonal mouse anti-human histone H1 -LRB- 1:1,000 ; Santa Cruz -RRB-, monoclonal mouse anti-GFP -LRB- 1:10,000, Roche -RRB- ; monoclonal mouse anti-eukaryote O-GlcNAc CTD110 .6 -LRB- 1:1,000 ; Hiss Diagnostics, Freiburg, Germany -RRB-, and monoclonal mouse anti-human glyceraldehyde-3-phosphate dehydrogenase -LRB- GAPDH ; 1:70,000, Millipore, Schwalbach, Germany -RRB-.
The monoclonal rat anti-Tat immunoglobulin G2a -LRB- IgG2a -RRB- antibody -LRB- clone 1C9 ; 1:150 -RRB- was produced by immunization of LOU/C rats with His-tagged purified recombinant Tat protein -LRB- 50 µg -RRB- according to a previously described procedure -LRB- 48 -RRB-.
The secondary, horseradish peroxidase-coupled antibodies goat anti-rat IgG, donkey anti-rabbit IgG, sheep anti-mouse IgG, and rabbit anti-goat IgG -LRB- all from Dako, Hamburg, Germany -RRB- were diluted 1:5,000.
Fractionation was performed with a nuclear/cytosol fractionation kit -LRB- BioVision, Wiesbaden, Germany -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's protocol -LRB- 64 -RRB-.
For gel shift experiments, cells were counted, and the nuclear fractions were lysed in 10 µl nuclear extraction buffer per 1 × 106 HEK 293T cells in order to concentrate the fractions.
The protein concentration was determined as described above.
Equal protein amounts of each fraction were loaded onto the gel and analyzed by Western blotting or applied to gel shift experiments.
HEK 293T cells -LRB- 2 × 106 -RRB- were seeded in 9 ml medium in 10-cm cell culture dishes.
The cells were transfected 24 h later -LRB- via the calcium phosphate method -RRB- with pcDNA4, pcDNA-Sp1, or pcDNA-Sp1 and pcDNA-OGT.
The total transfected DNA amount was adjusted to 30 µg with the control plasmid pcDNA4.
At 24 h after transfection, cells were washed with PBS and subsequently lysed in IP lysis buffer -LRB- 20 mM Tris-HCl, pH 7.5, 150 mM NaCl, 5 mM MgCl2, and 1 % Igepal -LSB- all purchased from Sigma-Aldrich -RSB- -RRB-, supplemented with one tablet of Complete Mini, EDTA-free protease inhibitor cocktail -LRB- Roche -RRB- per 10 ml.
The protein concentration was determined, and 1 mg total protein in a maximal volume of 1 ml was used for the immunoprecipitation.
The lysates were precleared by incubation with 100 µl Sepharose CL-6B -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB- at 4 ° C for 1 h..
The Sp1 protein complex was immunoprecipitated at 4 ° C for 3 h with 30 µg anti-Sp1 Pep2 antibody covalently coupled to agarose beads -LRB- Santa Cruz Biotechnology -RRB-.
Bead-coupled protein complexes were washed twice with 1 ml IP lysis buffer and three times with IP wash buffer -LRB- 20 mM Tris-HCl, pH 7.5, 150 mM NaCl, 5 mM MgCl2, and 0.1 % Igepal -RRB-.
The immunoprecipitates were analyzed by SDS-polyacrylamide gel electrophoresis and Western blotting as described above.
HEK 293T cells were seeded 24 h prior to transfection in 1.5 ml medium at a density of 3 × 105 cells per well in a six-well plate.
Cells were transiently cotransfected -LRB- via the calcium phosphate method -RRB- in triplicate with 0.5 µg pXP1-LTR-Sp1wt-Luc or 0.5 µg pEF1α-Luc, along with 0.75 µg pcDNA-Sp1 and/or 0.25 µg pCEP4-Tat and 1 µg pcDNA-OGT -LRB- unless otherwise indicated -RRB-.
The total DNA amount was adjusted to 2.5 µg with the control plasmid pcDNA4.
For RNA interference experiments, 0.22 µg -LRB- amount corresponds to 10 nM -RRB- short interfering RNA -LRB- siRNA -RRB- oligonucleotides specific for human OGT -LRB- hsOGT_7 SI02665131 ; Qiagen -RRB-, human Sp1 -LRB- hsSP1_1 SI00150976 ; Qiagen -RRB-, or human GAPDH -LRB- Silencer GAPDH siRNA ; Ambion, Darmstadt, Germany -RRB-, or a nontargeting control siRNA -LRB- Silencer Negative Control no. 1 siRNA ; Ambion -RRB- was cotransfected.
Twenty-four hours later, cells were lysed in 200 µl 1 × passive lysis buffer -LRB- Promega -RRB- and assayed for luciferase activity as described below.
Stable transfection of HEK 293T cells with pcDNA4-LTRwt-d2EGFP and pcDNA4-LTRmutSp1-d2EGFP was performed via the calcium phosphate method.
Stably transfected cells were selected with 600 µg / ml Zeocin -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB-.
After 10 days, single colonies were transferred to new culture plates.
Fluorescence intensity of clones was analyzed by flow cytometry.
For the final experiment, three clones of each construct, which expressed comparable fluorescence intensities, were selected.
Electroporation of Jurkat cells was performed with the Nucleofector II -LRB- Amaxa/Lonza, Cologne, Germany -RRB-.
Therefore, cells were resuspended in 100 µl Nucleofector solution V at a final concentration of 2 × 107 cells/ml and mixed with 50 µg / ml DNA -LRB- pcDNA4-EF1α-d2EGFP or pcDNA4-OGT -RRB-.
Electroporation was carried out with 100 µl cell DNA suspension using program X-001.
Immediately after transfection, cells were transferred to prewarmed RPMI 1640 medium supplemented with 10 % FCS and 4 mM l-glutamine.
At 48 h posttransfection, stably transfected Jurkat cells were selected with 400 µg / ml Zeocin -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB-.
After initial selection, cells were singularized by limited dilution into 96-well plates.
After 13 days, d2EGFP-expressing Jurkat clones were pooled, while OGT-expressing Jurkat clones were cultivated separately.
T lymphocytes were electroporated as described previously -LRB- 65 -RRB-.
Briefly, cells were washed once with pure RPMI 1640 and once with OptiMEM without phenol red -LRB- Invitrogen -RRB- -LRB- all at room temperature -RRB-.
The cells were resuspended in OptiMEM at a concentration of 1 × 108 cells/ml.
RNA was transferred to a 4-mm cuvette -LRB- Molecular Bioproducts, San Diego, CA -RRB- at a final concentration of 150 µg / ml.
A volume of 100 µl of cell suspension was added and immediately pulsed in a Gene Pulser Xcell -LRB- Bio-Rad -RRB-.
Pulse conditions for CD4 + T lymphocytes were square-wave pulse, 500 V, and 5 ms..
Immediately after electroporation, cells were transferred to prewarmed MLPC medium.
Cell lysates were centrifuged at 10,000 × g at 4 ° C for 3 min.
Firefly luciferase activity of the supernatants was measured using the luciferase assay system -LRB- Promega -RRB- in a Luminoskan Ascent instrument -LRB- Thermo Fisher Scientific, Langenselbold, Germany -RRB-.
Each luciferase reporter gene assay was performed in triplicate -LRB- except for that shown in Fig. 3 -RRB-.
OGT inhibits HIV-1 LTR promoter activity in infected primary CD4 + T cells.
Primary CD4 + T cells from two different donors were infected with VSV-G env pseudotyped HIV-1NL4-3LucR-E -.
At 36 h postinfection, cells were electroporated with in vitro-transcribed polyadenylated mRNA encoding either EGFP or OGT.
-LRB- A -RRB- At 8 h postelectroporation, luciferase activity was measured.
-LRB- B -RRB- The O-GlcNAcylation pattern and overexpression of EGFP and OGT were verified by Western blotting.
Staining of GAPDH demonstrates equal loading of proteins.
HEK 293T cells were transfected with the expression constructs for Sp1, OGT, or both, and nuclear proteins were isolated as already described.
The electrophoretic mobility shift assay was essentially performed as described previously -LRB- 54, 56 -RRB-.
Briefly, binding reaction mixtures -LRB- final volume, 15 µl -RRB- contained 10 mM Tris-HCl -LRB- pH 7.5 -RRB-, 80 mM NaCl, 1 mM EDTA, 1 mM dithiothreitol, 5 % glycerol, 3 µg of poly -LRB- dI-dC -RRB- · poly -LRB- dI-dC -RRB- -LRB- GE Healthcare -RRB-, 10 µg of nuclear extract, and 4 × 104 cpm of the 32P-end-labeled double-stranded oligonucleotide probe.
The oligonucleotides corresponded either to the wild-type HIV-1 LTR region containing the three binding sites for Sp1 -LRB- wt LTR-Sp1, 5' - GGATCGGGAGCGTGGCCTGGGCGGGACTGGGGAGTGGCGAGCCC-3' ; Sp1-binding sites are underlined -RRB- or to the Sp1-binding-site-mutated HIV-1 LTR -LRB- mut LTR-Sp1, 5' - GGATCGGGATTCGTGGCCTGTTCGGGACTGGTTAGTGGCGAGCCC-3' ; nucleotide substitutions in bold -RRB-.
After incubation for 45 min on ice, the protein-DNA complexes were resolved on nondenaturing 5 % polyacrylamide gels run in 1 × Tris-borate-EDTA buffer containing 89 mM Tris, 89 mM boric acid, and 2 mM EDTA -LRB- pH 8.0 -RRB-.
For competition experiments, a 10 -, 20 -, or 50-fold molar excess of unlabeled competitor oligomers was added to the gel shift mixtures prior to the addition of the 32P-labeled oligonucleotide probe and incubated for 30 min at 4 ° C..
For supershift assays, antibodies directed against Sp1, O-GlcNAc, or OGT were added to the gel shift mixture and incubated for 30 min at 4 ° C prior to the addition of the labeled probe.
Supershift antibodies were Sp1 Pep2 sc-59X -LRB- Santa Cruz Biotechnology -RRB-, O-GlcNAc CTD110 .6 -LRB- Hiss Diagnostics -RRB-, and OGT TI-14 -LRB- Sigma-Aldrich -RRB-, as well as IgG -LRB- NF-κB p50 sc114X -LSB- Santa Cruz Biotechnology -RSB- -RRB- and IgM -LRB- heparan sulfate 370255 -LSB- Seikagaku Corporation -RSB- -RRB- isotype controls.
All experiments were repeated three times.
One representative gel shift of each assay is shown.
RNA was isolated with RNeasy columns -LRB- Qiagen GmbH, Hilden, Germany -RRB- according to the manufacturer 's instructions.
RNA quality was verified by agarose gel electrophoresis, and RNA concentration was measured spectrophotometrically.
Reverse transcription of total RNA and amplification of OGT and GAPDH cDNA were performed as described previously -LRB- 53, 72 -RRB-.
PCR was carried out in a total reaction volume of 25 µl with 1 µl of either undiluted -LRB- 1 -RRB- or diluted -LRB- 1:5 and 1:10 -RRB- cDNA.
Primers specifically amplifying recombinant OGT were selected : the forward primer recognized specifically the vector-encoded 5' untranslated region of the recombinant OGT mRNA -LRB- 5' - TCCAGTGTGGTGGAATTCTG-3' -RRB- ; the reverse primer was homologous to a sequence corresponding to the N-terminal region of both endogenous and recombinant OGT -LRB- 5' - TTGCGTCTCAATTGCTTTCA-3' -RRB-.
Amplification of GAPDH was performed using the forward primer 5' - AGCCACATCGCTCAGAACAC-3' and the reverse primer 5' - GAGGCATTGCTGATGATCTTG-3' as described previously -LRB- 44 -RRB-.
Statistical significances were calculated with the Student t test for paired samples using the SPSS 15.0 and 16.0 software for Microsoft Windows -LRB- SPSS Inc., Chicago, IL -RRB-.
P values smaller than 0.05 were considered statistically significant -LRB- * -RRB-, P values smaller than 0.01 were considered highly significant -LRB- ** -RRB-, and P values smaller than 0.001 were considered the most significant -LRB- *** -RRB-.
RESULTS.
In order to evaluate whether O-GlcNAcylation affects HIV-1 replication, Jurkat, T1, and primary CD4 + T lymphocytes were infected with HIV-1NL4-3LucR-E -, a replication-deficient HIV-1 clone pseudotyped with the envelope protein VSV-G.
Upon integration, this recombinant virus expresses the firefly luciferase gene driven by the HIV-1 LTR promoter.
Consequently, the luciferase activity in infected cells correlates with the rate of HIV-1 gene transcription.
Reporter-HIV-1-infected cells were either left untreated -LRB- 0 mM -RRB- or treated for 24 h with increasing concentrations of GlcN -LRB- 0.25 mM, 1 mM, 4 mM, and 16 mM -RRB-, and luciferase activity was measured.
GlcN significantly inhibited the HIV-1 gene transcription by more than 60 % in Jurkat cells and 50 % in T1 cells -LRB- Fig. 1A and B -RRB- without significantly decreasing cell viability -LRB- Fig. 1A and B -RRB-.
Western blot analyses using an antibody which recognizes O-GlcNAcylated proteins demonstrated increased O-GlcNAcylation upon GlcN treatment, whereas expression of OGT remained unchanged -LRB- Fig. 1C -RRB-.
Detection of GAPDH and actin demonstrated that equal amounts of protein were loaded.
Similar results were obtained in primary CD4 + T lymphocytes from two different donors -LRB- Fig. 1D and E -RRB-, although HIV-1 replication in donor 2 -LRB- Fig. 1E -RRB- was inhibited to a lesser extent than was that in donor 1 -LRB- Fig. 1D -RRB-.
This difference is also reflected in smaller amounts of O-GlcNAcylated proteins in the lysates of donor 2 than in lysates of donor 1 -LRB- compare donor 1 and donor 2 in Fig. 1F, upper panel -RRB-.
GlcN inhibits HIV-1 transcription in lymphocytes.
Jurkat cells -LRB- A -RRB-, T1 cells -LRB- B -RRB-, and primary CD4 + T cells from two different donors -LRB- D and E -RRB- were infected with VSV-G env pseudotyped HIV-1NL4-3LucR-E - and cultured in the absence -LRB- 0 mM -RRB- or presence of different concentrations of GlcN -LRB- 0.25 mM, 1 mM, 4 mM, and 16 mM -RRB- for 24 h..
Subsequently, HIV-1 LTR-driven luciferase activity was measured -LRB- solid lines -RRB-.
The effect of GlcN on cytotoxicity and proliferation was monitored by MTT assay -LRB- dashed lines -RRB-.
The results are presented in terms of percent activities of untreated control cells.
The means ± standard deviations from triplicate determinations are indicated.
P values are calculated in comparison with control : *, P ≤ 0.05 ; **, P ≤ 0.
01. -LRB- C and F -RRB- Western blot analyses of O-GlcNAcylated proteins and OGT in Jurkat and T1 cells -LRB- C -RRB- and in primary CD4 + T lymphocytes -LRB- F -RRB-.
Actin and GAPDH served as loading controls.
Therefore, HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells, which stably express d1EGFP under the control of the HIV-1 LTR, were either left untreated -LRB- 0 mM -RRB- or treated with increasing concentrations of GlcN -LRB- 0.25 mM, 1 mM, 4 mM, and 16 mM -RRB-.
Subsequently, fluorescence intensity was measured by flow cytometry.
GlcN treatment inhibited the HIV-1 LTR-triggered d1EGFP expression in a dose-dependent manner, as detected by the shift of the fluorescence emission peak to a lower fluorescence intensity -LRB- Fig. 2A, bar diagram -RRB-.
Quantification of the different values demonstrated that GlcN significantly decreased the HIV-1 LTR activity by more than 60 % -LRB- Fig. 2A, bar diagram -RRB-.
Comparable results were obtained after treatment of HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells with the UDP-GlcNAc analog streptozotocin -LRB- data not shown -RRB-, which inhibits the O-GlcNAcase activity and thereby increases O-GlcNAcylation -LRB- 63 -RRB-.
GlcN inhibits HIV-1 LTR promoter activity and increases O-GlcNAcylation in HeLa cells.
-LRB- A -RRB- HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells were either left untreated -LRB- 0 mM -RRB- or stimulated for 5 h with increasing concentrations of GlcN -LRB- 0.25 mM, 1 mM, 4 mM, and 16 mM -RRB-.
The HIV-1 LTR activity was assessed by measuring the d1EGFP fluorescence intensity -LRB- FI -RRB- with flow cytometry analyses.
The shift of the fluorescence emission peak -LRB- inset -RRB- and the bar diagram of the respective geometric mean values compared to those for unstimulated control cells are shown.
The means ± standard deviations calculated from triplicate determinations are indicated.
P values are given for comparison with control : n.s., not significant ; **, P ≤ 0.01 ; ***, P ≤ 0.
001. -LRB- B -RRB- Nuclear and cytosolic fractions of unstimulated -LRB- control -RRB- or stimulated -LRB- 16 mM GlcN -RRB- HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells were analyzed by Western blotting to detect O-GlcNAcylated proteins.
Arrowheads mark proteins whose O-GlcNAcylation patterns are increased upon GlcN treatment.
Staining of OGT -LRB- an example of an O-GlcNAcylated protein -RRB- and histone H1 -LRB- non-O-GlcNAcylated -RRB- shows that protein expression levels were not altered.
Staining of GAPDH and lamin A/C demonstrates successful fractionation.
To demonstrate O-GlcNAcylation of cellular proteins in the presence of GlcN, cytosolic and nuclear fractions of control-treated versus GlcN-treated -LRB- 16 mM -RRB- HeLa-Tat-III/LTR/d1EGFP cells were analyzed by Western blotting -LRB- Fig. 2B -RRB-.
In both fractions, several proteins showed increased O-GlcNAcylation upon GlcN treatment -LRB- Fig. 2B, upper panels -RRB-, whereas the expression of OGT -LRB- example of an O-GlcNAc-modified protein -RRB- and of histone H1 -LRB- non-O-GlcNAc-modified protein -RRB- remained unchanged -LRB- Fig. 2B, middle panels -RRB-.
Successful fractionation of cytoplasmic and nuclear proteins and loading of equal protein amounts were verified by staining of lamin A/C and GAPDH -LRB- Fig. 2B, lower panels -RRB-.
Altogether, these results demonstrate that GlcN treatment enhances O-GlcNAcylation of cytoplasmic and nuclear proteins and that this correlates with decreased gene expression from the HIV-1 LTR promoter.
Since OGT is the only known enzyme to mediate O-GlcNAcylation, we investigated the effect of OGT on HIV-1 transcription in primary lymphocytes.
To this goal, primary CD4 + T lymphocytes from two different donors were infected with pseudotyped reporter HIV-1.
At 36 h postinfection the cells were transfected with in vitro-transcribed polyadenylated mRNA encoding either EGFP or OGT.
OGT expression levels were maximal at 8 h after transfection -LRB- data not shown -RRB-, and the cells were harvested.
Reporter analyses showed that overexpression of OGT inhibited HIV-1 transcription to an extent similar to that of treatment with 16 mM GlcN -LRB- compare Fig. 3A with Fig. 1D and E -RRB-.
The inhibition was slightly stronger in the cells of donor 2 than in the cells of donor 1, which correlated well with the increased OGT expression and O-GlcNAcylation level observed in the cells of donor 2 -LRB- Fig. 3B, upper panels ; compare donor 1 and donor 2 -RRB-.
Binding sites for both factors constitute the core promoter/enhancer of HIV-1, and both have been reported to be modified by O-GlcNAc -LRB- 21, 31 -RRB-.
In order to prove this hypothesis, luciferase reporter assays were performed using LTR reporters lacking the upstream modulatory region but containing the NF-κB - and/or Sp1-binding sites -LRB- either combined or isolated -RRB-, as well as a TATA box and the trans-activation response -LRB- TAR -RRB- element for Tat-mediated activation -LRB- Fig. 4A, LTR-κB-Sp1wt, LTR-κB-Sp1mut, and LTR-Sp1wt -RRB-.
HEK 293T cells were cotransfected with the reporter constructs and a Tat-encoding plasmid, along with an OGT-encoding plasmid or a control plasmid -LRB- Fig. 4B -RRB-.
Overexpression of OGT inhibited the Tat-induced activity of the promoters containing functional Sp1-binding sites -LRB- Fig. 4B, LTR-κB-Sp1wt and LTR-Sp1wt -RRB-.
In contrast, the activity of the promoter containing mutated Sp1-binding sites was increased upon overexpression of OGT -LRB- Fig. 4B, LTR-κB-Sp1mut -RRB-.
The transient expression of Tat itself was not significantly affected by overexpression of OGT -LRB- Fig. 4B, lower panels -RRB-.
The presence of Sp1-binding sites in the HIV-1 LTR promoter is required for OGT-mediated inhibition.

The effect of GlcN -LRB- 16 mM -RRB- on the HIV-1 LTR was analyzed by flow cytometry, and the mean fluorescence intensity is represented in the bar diagram.

Western blot analyses of one representative clone verify the increased O-GlcNAcylation pattern upon GlcN treatment and constant OGT expression.
GAPDH staining demonstrates that equal amounts of protein were loaded.
In a next step, the role of the Sp1-binding sites in the full-length HIV-1 LTR integrated into the cellular genome was analyzed.
Toward this goal, HEK 293T cells were stably transfected with plasmids expressing d2EGFP either under the control of the full-length wild-type HIV-1 LTR -LRB- Fig. 4C, LTRwt -RRB- or under the control of the full-length LTR containing mutated Sp1-binding sites -LRB- Fig. 4C, LTRmutSp1 -RRB-.
Three independent HEK 293T cell clones with similar fluorescence intensities were either left untreated or stimulated with 16 mM GlcN.
Subsequently, the promoter activities were measured by flow cytometry.
Mutation of the Sp1-binding sites strongly decreased HIV-1 LTR activity -LRB- Fig. 4D, compare fluorescence intensities in the bar diagram -RRB-.
However, GlcN treatment significantly decreased the fluorescence intensity only in cells expressing d2EGFP under the control of the wild-type HIV-1 LTR and had no significant effect on cells expressing d2EGFP under the control of the Sp1-mutated HIV-1 LTR -LRB- Fig. 4D, bar diagram -RRB-.
Western blot analyses demonstrated that GlcN treatment similarly increased the O-GlcNAcylation pattern in the two cell types, that OGT expression was not altered, and that equal amounts of proteins were loaded -LRB- Fig. 4D, right panels -RRB-.
Altogether these results demonstrate that the Sp1-binding sites are required for the GlcN-mediated inhibition of the full-length HIV-1 promoter integrated into the cellular genome.
To this goal, the sensitivity of the Tat-induced LTR-Sp1wt promoter to OGT was analyzed in HEK 293T cells in the absence and presence of Sp1.
Sp1 was recombinantly overexpressed, and its expression was inhibited with a specific siRNA.
A nontargeting siRNA was used as control.
Cotransfection of the control siRNA did not affect the OGT-mediated inhibition of the LTR-Sp1wt -LRB- Fig. 5A, compare bars 3 and 4 -RRB-.
Tat-mediated activation of the LTR-Sp1wt was less pronounced after knockdown of Sp1 -LRB- Fig. 5A, compare protein content-normalized relative light unit values given above bars 3 and 7 -RRB-.
However, OGT clearly did not inhibit LTR-Sp1wt promoter activity under these conditions -LRB- Fig. 5A, compare bars 7 and 8 -RRB-.
The expression of OGT and Tat was not altered upon depletion of Sp1 expression -LRB- Fig. 5B -RRB-.
Thus, in addition to the Sp1-binding sites, the presence of the Sp1 protein itself is also necessary for the OGT-mediated inhibition of the HIV-1 LTR activity.
Sp1 is crucial for the inhibitory effect of OGT on the HIV-1 LTR.

The GAPDH staining demonstrates that equal amounts of protein were loaded.
For this purpose, Sp1 was expressed alone or in combination with OGT -LRB- Fig. 6A, input -RRB-.
Immunoprecipitation experiments demonstrated that O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 was substantially increased when OGT was overexpressed -LRB- Fig. 6A, Sp1-IP -RRB-.
Coimmunoprecipitations revealed that OGT physically interacts with Sp1 under these conditions -LRB- data not shown -RRB-.
O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 selectively inhibits HIV-1 LTR promoter activity in a dose-dependent manner.

The latter triggers the expression of the housekeeping gene EF1α and harbors Sp1-binding sites.
Unlike the LTR-Sp1wt promoter, the EF1α promoter has no TAR element.
In order to ensure comparable induction levels, both reporter promoters were activated with Sp1 alone -LRB- Fig. 6B -RRB-.
In agreement with the results above, overexpression of OGT significantly inhibited the Sp1-triggered expression of LTR-Sp1wt -LRB- Fig. 6B, LTR-Sp1wt -RRB-.
To this end, the reporter LTR-Sp1wt was cotransfected with Sp1 - and Tat-encoding constructs in HEK 293T cells together with increasing amounts of OGT-encoding plasmid -LRB- 0.05 µg, 0.2 µg, and 1 µg -RRB-.
OGT clearly inhibited dose dependently the HIV-1 LTR promoter activity -LRB- Fig. 6C -RRB-.
The impact of OGT on the nuclear translocation of Sp1 was investigated by comparing the nuclear amounts of Sp1 in cells expressing endogenous or increased levels of OGT.
OGT does not interfere with Sp1 expression and DNA binding of Sp1.

Addition of an anti-OGT antibody did not shift Sp1-C -LRB- Fig. 7D, lanes 8 to 10 -RRB-.
Isotype control anti-IgG -LRB- Fig. 7D, lane 11 -RRB- and anti-IgM -LRB- Fig. 7D, lane 12 -RRB- antibodies had no effect on Sp1-C.
These results demonstrate that increased O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 inhibits neither the ability of Sp1 to translocate into the nucleus nor the DNA-binding affinity of Sp1.
To confirm that the inhibition of the HIV-1 LTR is dependent on Sp1 O-GlcNAcylation, a specific siRNA was used to deplete the expression of OGT.
The specificity of the siRNA was verified with an OGT rescue mutant -LRB- resOGT -RRB- - encoding plasmid, which contains six silent nucleotide exchanges in the siRNA-binding site -LRB- Fig. 8A -RRB-.
Western blot analyses proved that overexpression of wild-type OGT -LRB- wtOGT -RRB- was inhibited in HEK 293T cells cotransfected with the wtOGT-specific siRNA -LRB- Fig. 8B, top panel, lanes 2 and 4 -RRB-, whereas expression of resOGT was not affected -LRB- Fig. 8B, top panel, lanes 3 and 5 -RRB-.
Staining of O-GlcNAc-modified proteins served as an additional control for the functionality of resOGT -LRB- Fig. 8B, middle panel -RRB-.
Sp1 O-GlcNAcylation is necessary for the inhibition of the HIV-1 LTR.

Applying these tools to test the effect of Sp1 O-GlcNAcylation on HIV-1 LTR, we showed that the promoter activity -LRB- Fig. 8C, bar 4 -RRB- was strongly reduced after overexpression of wtOGT or resOGT -LRB- Fig. 8C, bars 5 and 6 -RRB-.
Cotransfection of a control siRNA targeting GAPDH had no impact on the HIV-1 LTR activity -LRB- Fig. 8C, bars 7 and 8 -RRB-.
Knockdown of wtOGT restored the HIV-1 LTR activity -LRB- Fig. 8C, bar 9 -RRB-, whereas resOGT escaped silencing and was still able to suppress the promoter activity -LRB- Fig. 8C, bar 10 -RRB-.
These findings demonstrate that O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 is required for the inhibition of the HIV-1 LTR promoter by OGT.
In all previous experiments the O-GlcNAcylation level was increased after infection with HIV-1.
Jurkat cells were stably transfected with OGT or, as a control, with d2EGFP.
Expression of recombinant OGT in selected clones was confirmed by RT-PCR -LRB- Fig. 9A -RRB-.
The stably transfected cells were infected with VSV-G env pseudotyped HIV-1NL4-3LucR-E -, and HIV-1 LTR activity was determined by luciferase assay.
Of note, HIV-1 LTR activity was 40-fold lower in both OGT-overexpressing Jurkat cell clones than in control cells expressing d2EGFP -LRB- Fig. 9B -RRB-.
These results demonstrate that OGT is a potent inhibitor of HIV-1 LTR activity.
OGT overexpression prior to infection amplifies the inhibitory effect on HIV-1 replication.

DISCUSSION.
Regulation of gene expression by nutrients like glucose and glucosamine is well established -LRB- 20, 37, 52, 74 -RRB- and demonstrates that cellular transcription adapts to environmental and metabolic changes.
Viruses critically depend on the host cell metabolism -LRB- 29 -RRB-.
This directed us to investigate the impact of the monosaccharidic metabolite O-GlcNAc on HIV-1 gene expression.
We showed that increased O-GlcNAc levels inhibit HIV-1 transcription in human T-cell lines as well as in human primary CD4 + T lymphocytes.
First, we demonstrated that O - GlcNAc-mediated inhibition of HIV-1 transcription required the presence of Sp1-binding sites in the HIV-1 LTR promoter.
The Sp1-binding sites are well conserved throughout the lentiviral HIV-1 LTRs -LRB- 18 -RRB-, and mutation of one or more Sp1-binding sites in the basal HIV-1 LTR promoter leads to a strong delay in replication in human peripheral blood lymphocytes and in T-cell lines -LRB- 45, 58 -RRB-.
This is also reflected in our observations that mutation of the Sp1-binding sites decreases HIV-1 LTR activity in transiently and stably transfected cells.
But although Sp1-mutated HIV-1 LTR activity was still measurable and inducible, no significant O-GlcNAc-mediated inhibition of promoter activity was observed.
Second, the presence of the Sp1 protein was crucial for the inhibitory effect of O-GlcNAc on the HIV-1 LTR.
Inhibition of Sp1 expression with siRNA completely abolished OGT-mediated inhibition of HIV-1 LTR activity.
Interestingly, although Sp1 is implicated in the activation of a large number of genes, depletion of the ubiquitous transcription factor did not induce cytotoxicity.
This is in agreement with the observation of Philipsen and coworkers, who disrupted the mouse Sp1 gene and found that Sp1-deficient embryonic stem cells were viable and showed normal growth characteristics -LRB- 50 -RRB-.
Third, Sp1 was found to be O-GlcNAcylated by OGT, and this decreased its ability to activate the HIV-1 LTR promoter.
These findings are in accordance with the results of Kudlow and colleagues, who showed that O-GlcNAcylation decreases the capability of Sp1 to activate GC-box-containing promoters -LRB- 77 -RRB-.
But it has to be emphasized that O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 does not generally inhibit transcription.
We have shown here that the human EF1α promoter, which also contains Sp1-binding sites -LRB- 55, 73, 75 -RRB-, is activated by O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1.
Additionally, others have shown that the expression of plasminogen activator inhibitor 1 -LRB- 14, 19, 20 -RRB-, calmodulin -LRB- 38 -RRB-, and argininosuccinate synthetase -LRB- 6, 7 -RRB- is also increased by Sp1 O-GlcNAcylation.
Thus, O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1 differentially modulates gene expression.
Furthermore, it has been shown that phosphorylation of distinct residues differentially regulates Sp1 activity -LRB- 5, 10, 11 -RRB-.
For example, O-GlcNAcylation reduces the ability of Sp1 to homomultimerize and to interact with transcriptional coactivator TATA-binding protein-associated factor II 110 -LRB- TAFII110 -RRB- -LRB- 62, 77 -RRB-.
These mechanisms are in accordance with our findings that O-GlcNAcylated Sp1 localizes at the HIV-1 LTR promoter and does not exhibit a decreased DNA-binding activity.
However, the transcription of the wild-type HIV-1 LTR -LRB- LTR-κB-Sp1wt -RRB- containing both NF-κB - and Sp1-binding sites was inhibited by O-GlcNAcylation of Sp1.
It has been reported that Sp1 can act as an anchor site for a repressor complex consisting of histone deacetylases and mSin3a -LRB- 82 -RRB-.
Intriguingly, Sp1 has also been detected in a DNA-protein complex with c-Myc and histone deacetylase 1 at the HIV-1 LTR, and it has been shown that this complex is involved in the establishment of proviral latency -LRB- 33 -RRB-.
This is supported by the fact that stable overexpression of OGT strongly inhibited replication of HIV-1 in de novo-infected lymphocytes.
Many reports have evaluated the effect of highly active antiretroviral therapy -LRB- HAART -RRB- on glucose metabolism -LRB- 15, 17, 49 -RRB- and the appearance of diabetes as a consequence of HAART -LRB- 40, 51 -RRB-.
But up to now, no studies have investigated the effect of glucose metabolism on HIV-1 replication.
Inactivation of Drosophila Huntingtin affects long-term adult functioning and the pathogenesis of a Huntington 's disease model.
SUMMARY.
To test these models, we generated a null mutant in the putative Drosophila HTT homolog -LRB- htt, hereafter referred to asdhtt -RRB- and, surprisingly, found that dhtt mutant animals are viable with no obvious developmental defects.
Instead, dhtt is required for maintaining the mobility and long-term survival of adult animals, and for modulating axonal terminal complexity in the adult brain.
INTRODUCTION.
Huntington 's disease -LRB- HD -RRB- is an autosomal dominant, progressive neurodegenerative disorder characterized clinically by deteriorating choreic movements, psychiatric disturbances and cognitive deficits -LRB- Gusella and MacDonald, 1995 ; Martin and Gusella, 1986 ; Vonsattel et al., 1985 -RRB-.
HD is caused by an abnormal expansion of a polyglutamine -LRB- polyQ -RRB- tract at the N-terminus of a large cytoplasmic protein, huntingtin -LRB- Htt -RRB- -LRB- The Huntington 's Disease Collaborative Research Group, 1993 -RRB-.
The polyQ tract contains between 6 and 35 repeats in the wild-type Htt protein, whereas it is expanded to beyond 36 repeats in HD -LRB- The Huntington 's Disease Collaborative Research Group, 1993 -RRB-.
Numerous studies have demonstrated that mutant Htt containing an expanded polyQ tract is toxic to neurons -LRB- Cattaneo et al., 2001 ; Gusella and MacDonald, 2000 -RRB-.
PolyQ expansion is also linked to at least eight other neurodegenerative disorders, collectively referred to as polyQ diseases -LRB- Riley and Orr, 2006 ; Zoghbi and Orr, 2000 -RRB-.
For example, mutant Htt can sequester wild-type Htt into insoluble aggregates, thereby exerting a dominant negative effect -LRB- Huang et al., 1998 ; Kazantsev et al., 1999 ; Narain et al., 1999 ; Preisinger et al., 1999 ; Wheeler et al., 2000 -RRB-.
In addition, wild-type Htt can suppress the cell death induced by mutant polyQ-expanded Htt in vitro -LRB- Leavitt et al., 2001 ; Van Raamsdonk et al., 2005 -RRB-.
Since its identification, the normal function of Htt has been subject to extensive investigation -LRB- Cattaneo et al., 2001 ; Harjes and Wanker, 2003 -RRB-.
The murine Htt homolog -LRB- also known as Hdh -RRB- is essential during early mouse development, as Htt-null mice die during gastrulation at embryonic day 7.5 -LRB- Duyao et al., 1995 ; Nasir et al., 1995 ; Zeitlin et al., 1995 -RRB-.
Currently, little is known about the normal biological function of wild-type Htt -LRB- Cattaneo et al., 2005 -RRB-.
Htt encodes a large cytoplasmic protein of 350 kDa.
Structural analysis of Htt proteins identified the presence of many HEAT -LRB- huntingtin, elongation factor 3, the A subunit of protein phosphatase 2A and TOR1 -RRB- repeats, which are approximately 40-amino acid -LRB- a.a. -RRB- long structural motifs, composed of two anti-parallel helices, of unknown function -LRB- Andrade and Bork, 1995 -RRB-.
Functional studies in mammalian systems, mainly from protein interaction assays, have associated Htt with diverse cellular processes including : endocytosis ; modulation of synapse structure and synaptic transmission ; transcriptional regulation, especially of the brain-derived neurotrophic factor -LRB- BDNF -RRB- which is essential for the survival of the striatal neurons affected in HD ; axonal transport of BDNF and vesicles ; and apoptosis -LRB- Cattaneo et al., 2001 ; Cattaneo et al., 2005 ; Harjes and Wanker, 2003 ; Zuccato et al., 2001 ; Zuccato and Cattaneo, 2007 -RRB-.
Importantly, only a few of these proposed functions of Htt have been directly tested in vivo owing to the early embryonic lethality associated with Htt-null mutant mice.
In an extensive search for Htt homologs in other species, Li et al. -LRB- Li et al., 1999 -RRB- identified a single HTT homolog in Drosophila -LRB- htt, hereafter referred to as dhtt -RRB-.
By sequence comparison, the homologous regions between Drosophila and human Htt proteins are mainly located within five discrete areas, including three relatively large continuous regions and two small segments, that cover about one-third of the total protein length -LRB- supplementary material Fig. S1A -RRB-.
At the amino acid level, these homologous regions, which are comprised of about 1200 a.a. residues in Drosophila Htt -LRB- dHtt -RRB-, share around 24 % identity and 49 % similarity -LRB- Li et al., 1999 -RRB-.
For example, in terms of the protein size, both the Drosophila and human Htt proteins are unusually large and contain 3583 and 3144 a.a. residues, respectively -LRB- Li et al., 1999 -RRB-.
In addition, the regions with a relatively high level of conservation are not only clustered in large continuous stretches, but are also located in the same order and distributed over the entire length of the proteins.
Moreover, dhtt and mammalian HD genes share similar patterns of gene expression -LRB- Li et al., 1999 -RRB- -LRB- Fig. 1 -RRB-.
Interestingly, although an HTT homolog exists in Drosophila, no HTT-like gene has been found in other less complex eukaryote species such as C. elegans or the yeast S. cerevisiae -LRB- Li et al., 1999 -RRB-.
Ubiquitous expression of dhtt in Drosophila.
-LRB- A -- F -RRB- dhtt is widely expressed at a low level during Drosophila development, as revealed by whole-mount in situ hybridization.

-LRB- C -- F -RRB- Third instar larval tissues hybridized with dhtt antisense probes.
Low-level and ubiquitous dhtt expression was observed in the brain -LRB- C -RRB-, wing and leg -LRB- D -RRB- and eye imaginal discs -LRB- E -RRB-.
-LRB- F -RRB- A negative in situ control -- an eye imaginal disc from a dhtt deletion mutant stained in parallel -- showed only minimal background signals.
-LRB- G -- K -RRB- The dHtt protein predominantly localizes to the cytoplasm.
-LRB- G, H -RRB- In transfected Drosophila S2 cells, ectopically expressed dHtt protein -LRB- green -RRB- was found predominantly in the cytoplasm ; it was also found on cellular protrusions, but was mostly excluded from the nucleus.
-LRB- G -RRB- Overlaying images of the S2 cells co-stained with phalloidin -LRB- red -RRB-, which detects F -- actin, and the DNA dye DAPI -LRB- blue -RRB- reveal the overall cell morphology and the cell nuclei, respectively.
